    Every person, firm, partnership, or corporation engaging in the activity described in section 22-234 shall keep a record containing a clear and accurate description of each item purchased sufficient to enable a reasonable person/law enforcement agent to identify the item (including specifically all identifying marks such as words, names, or initials), the date and amount of money paid for each item, the name of the seller, the social security or driver's license number of the seller, and the residence address (not general delivery or post office box, but including the box number if on any rural route) and the telephone number of the seller. The seller and the purchaser shall both sign the record of each transaction. On each day the purchaser transacts business of the type described herein he shall deliver to the chief of police a duplicate copy of the record concerning that day's business. This record shall be delivered by 12:00 noon of the day following the date of said transaction and by 12:00 noon on Monday for all transactions since the preceding Friday. The record shall be carefully preserved without any alteration and shall be at all times available for inspection by a police officer. 
(Ord. No. 567, § 6, 9-12-2011) 
Secs. 22-240-22-256. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - PAWNBROKERS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Alabama Pawnshop Act, MCL 5-19A-1 et seq. 

Sec. 22-257. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Pawnbroker means any person engaged in the business of lending money on the security of pledged goods left in pawn, or the business of purchasing tangible personal property to be left in pawn on the condition that it may be redeemed or repurchased by the seller for a fixed price within a fixed period of time. 
    Secondhand dealer means any person who buys, sells, or barters in secondhand goods and is subject to the licensing requirements of a "pawnbroker" or "salvage yard, salvage dealer, waste disposal, or recycling," and/or any person not subject to such license classifications who is engaged in the business of buying, selling, trading, or bartering in secondhand goods, and/or any person who is a pawnbroker under the Alabama Pawnshop Act (MCL 5-19A-1 et seq.). 
    Secondhand goods means any property of any kind or description which has been previously sold to or owned by a consumer or other person who is not a merchant as defined by Code of Ala. 1975, § 7-2-104, or that constitutes pledged goods under the Alabama Pawnshop Act, or that is sold or received as scrap or salvage property, provided that the household furnishings, clothing, waste, and animal waste or aluminum drink cans shall not be considered secondhand goods within this article. 
(Ord. No. 585, § 1, 1-12-2015) 
Sec. 22-258. - Business license. 
    Each person registering as a pawnbroker must comply with the licensing requirements of the Alabama Pawnshop Act (MCL 5-19A-1 et seq.) and obtain a business license from the city. 
(Ord. No. 585, § 2, 1-12-2015) 
Sec. 22-259. - Reports to the chief of police. 
(a)  Every pawnbroker within the city limits shall electronically report to the chief of police a description of every article or thing received by him in pawn, pledge, trade, purchase or consignment. Transaction reports may be entered as soon as time will allow. All transaction reports must be submitted within seven calendar days following said transaction date. 
(b)  Computerized reporting of pawnshop information shall be mandatory. The chief of police shall establish the format and requirements for the transmission of data and may restrict the scope of the items that are to be electronically reported. A transaction reported by electronic transmission under this section shall not be reported on paper forms unless the police chief requests such. Each pawnbroker may pay a fee of $0.50 per transaction required to be electronically reported, if the electronic report transmitted to the chief of police is erroneous, duplicative or in an incorrect or incompatible format, or if no electronic report of the transaction is transmitted. 
(c)  Pawnbrokers shall report their transactions electronically to the police chief as required by this section from and after the following dates: 
(1)  For each pawnshop for which a pawnbroker license is first obtained on or after the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived, effective upon commencing business. 
(2)  For each pawnshop for which a pawnbroker license was first obtained before the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived that maintains a computerized record-keeping system for its own record of transactions, no later than 45 days after the adoption of the ordinance from which this section is derived. 
(3)  For each pawnshop for which a pawnbroker license was first obtained before the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived, not later than 45 days. 
(d)  The chief of police may, for good cause shown, grant a pawnbroker an extension of the deadline to a date not later than ten days. An extension may only be granted upon written application by the pawnbroker and upon a showing that the pawnbroker is making satisfactory progress toward acquiring computer programs and equipment to make the necessary electronic transmission of all transactions of the pawnshop. 
(e)  If, after establishing the format and requirements for the transmission of computerized reports of transactions, the chief of police alters the required format, pawnbrokers shall be given at least 45 days to comply with the new format requirements. 
(Ord. No. 585, § 4, 1-12-2015) 
Sec. 22-260. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person found guilty of violating any provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(b)  After notice and hearing, a pawnbroker's municipal business license may be suspended or revoked upon finding that one or more of the following have occurred: 
(1)  The pawnbroker licensee either knowingly or without the exercise of due care has violated this article. 
(2)  A fact or condition exists which, if it had been known at the time of the original application for a license, would have justified the refusal to issue a license. 
(3)  The pawnbroker/licensee has aided, abetted or conspired with an individual or person to circumvent the requirements of this article. 
(4)  The licensee or a legal or beneficial owner of the license has been convicted of a crime involving moral turpitude. 
(5)  Has intentionally not accurately reported the information required under Code of Ala. 1975, § 5-19A-1 and/or the provisions of this article. 
(c)  A hearing officer may conditionally license or place on probation a person whose license has been suspended or may reprimand a licensee for violation of this article. 
(d)  A hearing officer may reinstate a suspended license or issue a new license to a person whose license has been revoked if no fact or condition then exists which would have justified the refusal to originally issue a license. 
(e)  Hearing officers shall be designated as the chief of police, ordinance officer, revenue officer, one mayor appointee, and one council appointee. A quorum shall consist of no less than three of the aforementioned hearing officers. At least one appointee must be present and included within the quorum. 
(Ord. No. 585, § 5, 1-12-2015) 
Secs. 22-261-22-283. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - 2016 LODGING TAX[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- State transient occupancy tax, Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-26-1 et seq. 

Sec. 22-284. - Levy of tax in the city. 
    For the privilege of engaging or continuing within the city in the business activities hereinafter referred to, there is hereby levied, in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law, and shall be collected as hereinafter provided, an additional privilege or license tax against the person on account of the business activities and in the amount to be determined by the application of the rates against gross receipts as follows: 
    There is hereby levied and imposed, in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law, an additional privilege or license tax upon every person, firm, or corporation engaged in the business of renting or furnishing any rooms, lodgings, or accommodations to transients in any hotel, motel, inn, tourist camp, tourist cabin, or any other place in which rooms, lodgings or accommodations are regularly furnished to transients for a consideration, in the amount of two percent of the charge for such room, rooms, lodgings, or accommodations, including the charge for use or rental of personal property and services furnished in such rooms. Provided, however, there is exempted from the tax levied under the provisions of this article any rentals or sales taxed under the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, title 40, ch. 23, art. 1 (Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-1 et seq.). The tax shall not apply to rooms, lodgings, or accommodations supplied for a period of 30 continuous days or more in any place. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 1, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-285. - Levy of tax in police jurisdiction. 
    For the privilege of engaging or continuing in the business activities hereinafter referred to within the police jurisdiction of the city outside of its corporate limits, there is hereby levied, in addition to all taxes of every kind now imposed by law, and shall be collected as herein provided, an additional privilege or license tax against the persons on account of the business activities in the amounts to be determined by the application of rates against gross receipts as follows: 
    There is hereby levied and imposed in addition to all other taxes of every kind now imposed by law, an additional privilege or license tax on every person, firm, or corporation engaged in the business of renting or furnishing any rooms, lodgings, or accommodations to transients in any hotel, motel, inn, tourist camp, tourist cabin, or any other place in which rooms, lodgings or accommodations are regularly furnished to transients for a consideration, in the amount to be determined by the application of the rate of one percent of the charge for such room, rooms, lodgings, or accommodations, including the charge for use or rental of personal property and services furnished in such room. Provided, however, there is exempted from the tax levied under the provisions of this article any rentals or services taxed under the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, title 40, ch. 23, art. 1 (Code of Ala. 1975, § 40-23-1 et seq.). The tax shall not apply to rooms, lodgings or accommodations supplied for a period of 30 continuous days or more in any one place. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 2, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-286. - Provisions of state lodging tax statutes applicable to this article and taxes levied herein. 
    This article and the taxes herein levied shall be subject to all definitions, exceptions, exemptions, proceedings, requirements, rules, regulations, provisions, penalties, fines, punishments, and deductions that are applicable to the taxes levied by the state lodging tax statutes, except where inapplicable or where herein otherwise provided, including all the provisions of the state lodging tax statutes, for enforcement and collection of taxes. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 3, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-287. - Adding amount of tax to price. 
    Any person on whom the tax levied by this article is imposed may add the tax herein levied to the receipts from rental of rooms, lodgings or accommodations and may collect the same from the occupants of such rooms, but this section is not mandatory. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 4, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-288. - This article cumulative. 
    This article shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of the general license code or any other ordinances in the city, but shall be held to be cumulative, and the amounts of the taxes herein levied shall be in addition to the amounts of all other license taxes levied by the city by its general license code or any ordinances. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 5, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-289. - City tourism and economic development account established; tax to be paid into account. 
    There is hereby established a special city fund to be entitled the City Tourism and Economic Development Account from which the proceeds of this tax shall be paid into upon receipt. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 6, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-290. - Disbursements from city tourism and economic development account. 
(a)  The treasurer of the city shall pay out of said city tourism and economic development account, on a quarterly basis, one-fourth of the gross receipts of this tax to the commercial development authority of the city, one-fourth of the gross of this tax receipts to the downtown redevelopment authority of the city and one-half of the gross receipts of this tax into a special tourism grant fund. Grants from this fund shall to be awarded by vote of the city council after it has established an application process by resolution and with any grant to be voted for and approved in a public meeting of the city council. 
(b)  Any funds held in said city tourism and economic development account shall roll over each fiscal year into said account. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 7, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-291. - Continuation of expenditures. 
    The authorized expenditures above under this tax from the special fund shall continue for a period of five years after the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, at which time the city council may in its discretion change the funding formula. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 8, 4-26-2016) 
Sec. 22-292. - Exemption. 
    This article shall not apply and said tax shall not be imposed on RV or campsite rentals. 
(Ord. No. 590, § 11, 4-26-2016) 
Secs. 22-293-22-316. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - DOOR-TO-DOOR SALES OR SOLICITATIONS 

Sec. 22-317. - Declaration of intent. 
    The practice of going in and upon private residences, public buildings, and businesses in the city by solicitors, peddlers, hawkers, itinerant merchants, and transient vendors of goods, wares, merchandise, books, pictures, and periodicals, not having been requested or invited to do so by the owners or occupants of such private residences, public buildings or businesses for the purpose of soliciting orders for the sale of goods, wares, merchandise, books, pictures and periodicals or for the purpose of disposing of, or peddling or hawking the same, is hereby declared a nuisance and to be unlawful unless one has obtained a city registration certificate. 
Sec. 22-318. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Charity or nonprofit organization means any enterprise entered into with the primary purpose to pursue social, charitable, or other benevolent activities and that is classified as a tax-exempt organization under applicable provisions of the United States Internal Revenue Code and the regulations thereunder. To be classified as a tax-exempt organization, the organization must hold a tax-exempt certificate from the Internal Revenue Service. 
    Registrant or registered solicitor means any person who is subject to this article and who has obtained a valid certificate of registration from the city. 
    Residence means any living unit contained within any building or structure that is occupied by any person as a dwelling consistent with the definition of the term "residence" as defined in the zoning ordinance of the city. 
    Solicitation means any of the following activities: 
(1)  Seeking to obtain orders for the sale or exchange of goods, wares, merchandise, or perishables of any kind, for any kind of remuneration of consideration, regardless of whether advance payment is sought; 
(2)  Seeking to obtain prospective customers to apply for or to purchase insurance, publications or subscriptions to publications; 
(3)  Seeking to obtain contributions or donations of anything of value for the benefit of any individual, association, organization, corporation, or program; 
(4)  Seeking to obtain orders or prospective customers for goods or services; 
(5)  Requesting monies or contributions of other goods or services for any charity or nonprofit organization or for-profit organization or any other type or form of entity; 
(6)  Distributing handbills, written advertisements, or publications. 
    Solicitor means a person engaged in the activities defined in this article as soliciting. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 1, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-319. - Registration requirements for door-to-door solicitation. 
(a)  Registration. All persons desiring to engage in soliciting at residences in the city shall apply to the city at a cost of $300.00 yearly, paid in cash or cash equivalent, for a certificate of registration. The certificate, executed by the city clerk or his designee, shall be maintained by the city clerk and a legible copy shall be carried by the registrant at all times while soliciting. Upon request for inspection by an occupant of a residence or a police officer or a city license officer while the registered solicitor is transacting his business or seeking to transact his business at any residence, the registrant shall show his copy of the registration certificate. 
(b)  Application for certificate. The city shall provide a standard form for use for registration of solicitors. The applicant for the registration certificate shall state in writing upon his oath or affirmation that the information is truthfully provided to the best of his knowledge and belief. The applicant shall supply with or upon the registration form the following information: 
(1)  Applicant's true, correct, and legal name and the name of the organization for which he will be soliciting; 
(2)  Address and phone number of applicant's home and place of business; 
(3)  Names and addresses of the corporate officers or the partners and the managers, if any, of the entity for which the applicant will be soliciting; 
(4)  The purpose for which soliciting will be done; 
(5)  A brief description of the method of presentation that will be made; 
(6)  Whether a permit, license, or certificate of registration from any city in connection with soliciting has ever been revoked or suspended, explaining the circumstances; 
(7)  A statement as to whether or not the applicant has ever been convicted of a misdemeanor or a felony; 
(8)  Documentation that the person is authorized to solicit for the organization; 
(9)  Two passport-sized photos taken within 60 days of application. 
(c)  Police department notified of solicitation. The police department must be notified of the neighborhood in which the solicitation will take place, and the solicitor must remain in that neighborhood unless notification has been given to the police department of the change in neighborhood. 
(d)  Non-endorsement. In addition, the applicant shall certify on the application form that if his registration is granted, he will not state, imply, or represent to any person that the issuance of the certificate is an endorsement by the city of the product, service, solicitor, or the organization represented by the solicitor. 
(e)  Proof of identification required. No certificate of registration shall be issued except upon proof of identification, including a photograph of the applicant, in one of the following forms: 
(1)  A valid driver's license of any state in the United States. 
(2)  A valid United States Uniform Service Identification. 
(3)  A valid passport. 
(4)  A valid identification issued by any agency of a state for the purpose of identification of the holder. 
(f)  Registration complete with issuance. Registration shall be complete when the city issues the certificate of registration, which shall not be unreasonably withheld or delayed. 
(g)  Form of certificate. Each certificate shall be numbered, shall list the name of the individual solicitor and of all organizations on whose behalf he is authorized to solicit, the date on which the certificate will expire, and shall be dated and signed by the city clerk or his designee. 
(h)  Expiration. Certificates shall be valid until December 31 of the current year. 
(i)  Non-transferability. Certificates of registration shall be issued only in the name of the applicant and the firms, corporations or associations on whose behalf he is authorized to solicit. Each person soliciting must obtain a certificate of registration. Certificates shall be nontransferable. It shall be a violation for a solicitor whose certificate authorizes soliciting on behalf of a firm named in the certificate to solicit on behalf of any other firm, organization or association or for any purpose other than that specified on the application. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 2, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-320. - Exemptions from registration. 
    The registration provisions of this article do not apply to the following: 
(1)  Persons making solicitations solely for a church, religious organization or charitable organization, including any unincorporated association or corporation under the supervision and control of any church, charitable organization or religious organization, if the church or organization is tax-exempt under the provisions of the United States Internal Revenue Code. 
(2)  Students soliciting contributions to finance extracurricular academic, social, athletic, artistic, scientific, or cultural programs, provided that the solicitation and its purpose have been approved by the principal, president, or chief administrator of the school that the students attend. Any school, private and public, must be located within the county and is deemed to include Northeast Alabama Community College. 
(3)  Persons canvassing for the purpose of distributing political literature or materials on behalf of a political party, candidate, or public issue or introducing themselves as supporters of a candidate, political party, cause, or issue. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 3, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-321. - Deceptive soliciting practices prohibited. 
(a)  No solicitor or canvasser shall intentionally or recklessly make any materially false or fraudulent statement in the course of soliciting. 
(b)  No solicitor shall use a fictitious name, an alias, or any name other than his true, correct, and legal name. 
(c)  No solicitor shall represent, directly or by implication, that the city or any other governmental entity endorses the solicitation or that the granting of a certificate of registration implies any endorsement of the solicitor's produce, goods, wares, or services or of the individual solicitor. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 4, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-322. - No registration of felons. 
    No certificate of registration shall be issued to any person who has been convicted of a state or federal felony. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 5, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-323. - Revocation of certificate. 
    Any certificate of registration issued hereunder shall be revoked by the city if the registrant is convicted of a violation of this article, if the registrant has falsified the application, or otherwise becomes disqualified for the issuance of a certificate of registration. Notice of revocation shall be given to the registrant by personal service or by certified mail to the address listed on the application. Immediately upon the giving of such notice, the certificate of registration shall become null and void and shall remain so unless the revocation is ordered rescinded by the city clerk. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 6, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-324. - Appeal. 
    An applicant whose registration was denied or registrant whose certificate was revoked shall have the right to appeal to the city clerk. An applicant shall also have the right to appeal any adverse decision of the city clerk to the city council. Any appeal must be demanded in writing sent by certified mail to the city clerk within seven calendar days of the decision that is being appealed. The right of appeal to the city council is not in derogation of any other rights in law or equity the applicant might have. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 7, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-325. - Residential "no soliciting" notices. 
(a)  Any occupant of a residence or occupants of a multifamily dwelling who desires not to have solicitors call on said residences shall give notice of the desire to refuse solicitors by displaying a clearly visible weatherproof placard no smaller than 16 square inches and no larger than 94 square inches stating "No Soliciting" which shall be posted on or near the main entrance of the private property and not within the public right-of-way. 
(b)  Residents of a residential subdivision may indicate their desire not to have solicitors call on any residences in that subdivision by giving notice of the desire to refuse solicitors by displaying a clearly visible weatherproof placard no smaller than 16 square inches and no larger than 94 square inches stating "No Soliciting" which shall be posted on or near each entrance of the subdivision on private property and not within the public right-of-way. 
(c)  The display of said placard shall be deemed to constitute notice to any solicitor that the inhabitant of the residence does not desire to invite solicitors. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 8, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-326. - Duties of solicitors. 
(a)  Every solicitor shall, upon entering premises on which a residence is located, examine the main entrance to the premises for any "No Soliciting" placard, and if one is posted, desist in any efforts to solicit or to leave any literature concerning the solicitation at that residence. Possession of a certificate of registration does not relieve any solicitor of this duty. 
(b)  It is unlawful for any person to appear at any private residence and canvass or solicit whereon a placard bearing the words "No Soliciting" or words of similar import is posted for public view. Possession of a certificate of registration does not relieve any solicitor of this duty. 
(c)  Any solicitor who is asked to leave any residence by the occupant shall immediately and peacefully depart. Possession of a certificate of registration does not relieve any solicitor of this duty. 
(d)  Every solicitor shall at all times, while exercising the privilege in the city incident to the permit, carry upon his person his permit, and the same shall be exhibited by such person whenever he is requested to do so by any police officer or by any person who is solicited. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 9, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-327. - Time of day restrictions on soliciting. 
    It is a violation of this article for any person, whether registered or not, to solicit any person at his residence between 8:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 10, 7-28-2009) 
Sec. 22-328. - Solicitors properly identified. 
    All solicitors must be properly identified in the form of a removable name tag as supplied by the city at a cost of $0.25 per name tag with the solicitors name, company name and permit number. 
(Ord. No. 548, § 11, 7-28-2009) 
Chapter 23 - MANUFACTURED HOMES AND TRAILERS 

Sec. 23-1. - Building numbering, street naming and mobile parks. 
(a)  There is hereby established a uniform system for naming all streets and numbering all mobile home lots, fronting on all streets, avenues and public ways, within all mobile home parks in the city (limits - jurisdiction) and all lots shall be numbered in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(b)  All streets shall be named by the owner of each mobile home park. Each mobile home park owner shall be responsible for clearing the name of each street with the city planner or other person so designated by the mayor of the city, to ascertain that there is no other city street of like or similar name, before that name is officially affixed to said street. 
(c)  All lots on the right side proceeding from the end of each street nearest the main entrance of the mobile home park shall be even numbers. All lots on the left side proceeding from the end of each street nearest the main entrance of the mobile home park shall be odd numbers. 
(d)  There shall be assigned to each lot, its respective number under the uniform system provided for in this chapter. 
(e)  Such numbers shall be placed within 90 days after the passage of this chapter or after assigning of the proper number. The cost of the numbers shall be paid by the property owner. The numbers used shall not be less than 21/2 inches in height and shall be made of durable and clearly visible material. 
(f)  The numbers shall be conspicuously placed within 20 feet of the edge of the street on which the mobile home lot faces and shall be placed no less than 24 inches above the ground and no more than 48 inches. 
(Ord. No. 159, §§ 1-6, 2-14-1977) 
Chapter 24 - MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS AND OFFENSES 

Sec. 24-1. - Adoption of state offenses. 
(a)  Any person or corporation committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof, which is declared by state law now existing or hereafter enacted to be a misdemeanor, shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(b)  Any person or corporation committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(c)  Any person or corporation committing within the corporate limits of the city or within the police jurisdiction thereof an offense as defined by Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-1-2, which offense is not declared by state law now existing or hereafter enacted to be a felony, misdemeanor, or violation, shall be guilty of an offense against the city. 
(d)  Any person or corporation found to be in violation of subsections (a), (b) or (c) of this section shall, upon conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 593, 2-27-2017) 
Sec. 24-2. - Noise. 
(a)  It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue to make or cause to be made or continued to be made any loud or excessive noise which unreasonably interferes with the comfort, health or safety of other persons within the city. 
(1)  It is hereby declared a nuisance and shall be unlawful to operate or play any radio, musical instrument, phonographs or similar devices whether from a motor vehicle or by a pedestrian in such a manner as to be plainly audible to any person other than the player or operator of the device or passengers in the motor vehicle at a distance of 20 feet in the case of the motor vehicle or ten feet in the case of the pedestrian. 
(2)  It is hereby declared a nuisance and shall be unlawful to operate or play any radio, television, phonograph, musical instrument or similar device which produces or reproduces sound, whether from a business or residence, park, beach, or other similar place in such a manner as to be plainly audible at a distance of 50 feet to any person in a commercial, residential, multifamily dwelling or other public place. 
(b)  Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit special performances by a band or orchestra in a hall, building, or in the open air after proper permits have been obtained from the chief of police. Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit the ringing of church bells or chimes within the city or noises or sounds produced by radios, sirens or other equipment attached to or being operated by any police, fire, rescue or other emergency vehicles or personnel. 
(c)  Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit the conducting of live remote broadcast by duly licensed radio stations upon business premises at the request of the owner of the business. Said live remote broadcast shall be limited to daylight hours only. 
(Ord. No. 445, §§ 1, 3, 4, 5-24-1995) 
Chapter 26 - MUNICIPAL COURT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal court, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-1 et seq. 

Sec. 26-1. - Establishment of municipal court. 
    That there be and there is hereby established, effective December 27, 1977, a municipal court for the city pursuant to the provisions of Act 1205, 1975 Regular Session of the Alabama Legislature. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 1, 12-12-1977) 
Sec. 26-2. - Number of judges. 
    The municipal court shall consist of one municipal judge. 
State Law reference- Municipal judges generally, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-30 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 4, 12-12-1977) 
Sec. 26-3. - Compensation of judge. 
    The annual salary of the municipal judge of the city is as established from time to time by the council. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 5, 12-12-1977) 
State Law reference- Compensation of judge, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-33. 
Sec. 26-4. - Court costs generally. 
    Upon each conviction in the municipal court for a violation of any ordinance of the city there shall be taxed against the defendant as court costs the sum of $10.00, and there shall also be taxed as costs the additional costs and fees imposed by the statutes of the state, and the latter such costs and fees shall be remitted pursuant to the said statutes. All costs taxed for the city, as hereinabove provided, shall be paid into the city treasury. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 6(D), 12-12-1977) 
State Law reference- Court costs, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-14. 
Sec. 26-5. - Additional court costs. 
(a)  In addition to any and all court costs and fees now or hereafter authorized, an additional $5.00 court cost fee shall be assessed and collected on all the municipal court cases filed within the municipal court of the city. 
(b)  The additional court costs provided herein, when collected by the city, shall be paid to the following funds as follows: 
(1)  $4.00 to a capital fund for the municipal court payment of capital and equipment costs within the municipal court; and 
(2)  $1.00 into a fund for capital expenses for the city police department. 
(c)  The assessment of fees shall not be waived by any court unless all other fees, assessments, costs, fines, and charges associated with the case are waived. 
(Ord. No. 563, §§ 1-3, 11-22-2010) 
State Law reference- Court costs, Code of Ala. 1975, § 12-14-14. 
Sec. 26-6. - Additional court costs for crime victims' compensation fund. 
    In addition to costs and charges otherwise fixed by law upon conviction for violations of municipal ordinances, there is hereby imposed, pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 15-23-17, such convictions as follows: 
(1)  Traffic violations. $2.00, crime victims compensation fund. 
(2)  Non-traffic violations. $10.00, crime victims compensation fund. 
(Ord. No. 226, § 1, 6-25-1984) 
Sec. 26-7. - Reports generally. 
    The municipal judge shall report on the proceedings of the municipal court as required by law or rule. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 12, 12-12-1977) 
Sec. 26-8. - Reports to council. 
    The municipal judge shall be required to make a report to the council on the operation of the municipal court every month. 
(Ord. No. 166, § 13, 12-12-1977) 
Sec. 26-9. - Magistrate's fines schedule. 
(a)  Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Alabama Rules of Judicial Administration, the city does hereby amend its local schedule of fines established for the city municipal court where a defendant elects to plead guilty before a magistrate, the fine established in the schedule shall apply. (See Exhibit A, attached hereto by reference.) 
(b)  The procedure whereby a defendant in municipal court elects to plead guilty before a magistrate shall be those procedures established in Rule 20 of the Alabama Rules of Judicial Administration. 
(Ord. No. 412, exh. A, 7-12-1996; Ord. No. 495, 4-25-2005; Ord. No. 412-2, 11-22-2010) 
Sec. 26-10. - Failure to appear. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful and shall constitute a misdemeanor against the city for any person to fail to appear before the appropriate judge or magistrate in court pursuant to Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-1-4. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful and constitute a misdemeanor against the city for any person charged with any misdemeanor within the city or the police jurisdiction thereof under a municipal ordinance or state law adopted by the city, which shall be before the municipal court, to fail to appear before a judge or magistrate as required in connection with any misdemeanor. 
(c)  It is directed that the clerk of the court shall distribute monies paid into court on any charges or in any situation where failure to appear has taken place with monies received first paying toward any original fine and court costs; second to any fines under failure to appear charges are to be placed in a fund to be referred to as the Scottsboro Police FTA Account; and last, any court costs as required by the statutes of the state. 
(d)  This section shall not impact the right of a judge to cite a defendant who fails to appear with contempt pursuant to Rule 33.3 of the Alabama Rules of Criminal Procedure, nor does it prevent a judge from ordering the arrest of a probationary who fails to fulfill any condition of probation or initiate revocation proceedings against him pursuant to Rules 27.4, 27.5 and 26.11 of the Alabama Rules of Criminal Procedure. 
(Ord. No. 485, §§ 1, 2, 4, 5, 12-22-2003) 
Chapter 28 - NUISANCES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- General authority relative to nuisances and health and cleanliness, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-47-117 et seq. 

Sec. 28-1. - Junked, wrecked, and abandoned property. 
(a)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Abandoned property means all tangible personal property which does not have an identifiable owner and which has been disposed of on public property in a wrecked, inoperative or partially dismantled condition or which has no apparent value to its rightful owner. 
    Property means any real property within the city which is not a street or highway. 
    Street or highway means the entire width of right-of-way between boundary lines of every dedicated public right-of-way within the city. 
    Vehicle means a machine propelled by other than human power designed to travel along the ground on wheels, treads, runners or slides and transport persons or property and includes, without limitation, automobiles, trucks, trailers, wagons, tractors, motorcycles and buggies. 
(b)  No person shall abandon, store, park, leave or permit the storing of any vehicle within the city for such time and under such circumstances as to cause such vehicle to reasonably appear to have been abandoned. 
(c)  No person shall leave any partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked or junked vehicle on any street or highway in the city. 
(d)  No person in charge or control of any real property within the city, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee or otherwise shall allow any partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked, junked or discarded vehicle to remain on such property for longer than ten days. No person shall leave any abandoned property or vehicle on any property within the city for longer time than ten days. This section shall not apply to vehicles in an enclosed storage building, or vehicles in an appropriate storage place, depository or facility maintained in a lawful place and manner by the city. This section shall not apply to licensed and registered junkyards or automobile dealerships if said junkyards or automobile dealerships are licensed by the city. 
(e)  The placing and storage of vehicle's on public or private property as defined in subsection (a) of this section shall constitute a nuisance, detrimental to the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of the city. It shall be the duty of the owner of vehicles and the private property owner or lessee or such other person in possession of private property where such vehicle may be located to remove it from the city or to have it housed in an enclosed building where it shall not be visible from the street. 
(f)  Any police officer or an employee of the city, authorized by the mayor to do so, shall give written notice to the registered owner of the vehicle which is in violation of this chapter or to give such notice to the owner, lessee or person in possession of the property whereon the vehicle is situated if the identity of the registered owner is not readily ascertainable, advising such person that the vehicle violates this chapter and demanding that the vehicle be removed from the city within ten days or that within ten days it shall be housed in an enclosed building where it will not be visible from the street. Such notice shall be given by personal service or by certified mail. 
(g)  Junked motor vehicles having no apparent market value other than for salvage or parts or as scrap metal abandoned on any city street or public property in an inoperable condition are hereby declared to be a public nuisance, and any police officer or an employee of the city, authorized by the mayor to do so, is hereby authorized to summarily abate such nuisances by removing junked motor vehicles to protect the health, safety and welfare of the public. 
(h)  Before any vehicle may be sold or disposed of by the city all relevant provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, title 32, ch. 13 (Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-13-1 et seq.) shall be followed. 
(h)  This chapter is cumulative and shall not be construed as repealing, limiting or restriction any other ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. No. 415, §§ 1-8, 10, 2-24-1997) 
Sec. 28-2. - Demolition of buildings and structures. 
(a)  The city through its city council does hereby elect to come under the provisions of Code of Ala. 1975, title 11, ch. 40, art. 2 (Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-40-30 et seq.). 
(b)  The term "appropriate municipal official," for the purposes of this section, means the city's zoning adjustment board along with any other person designated by the mayor and council to exercise the authority and to perform the duties under that article referenced in subsection (a) of this section. 
(c)  This chapter is intended to be cumulative in nature and in addition to any power and authority in which the city already has adopted in regard to housing, buildings, weeds, junk and matters of this kind. 
Chapter 30 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Solid Waste Disposal Act, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-1 et seq.; local solid waste management programs, Code of Ala. 1975, § 22-27-47; criminal littering, Code of Ala. 1975, § 13A-7-29. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Litter control. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Approved, enclosed, covered structure means any building, garage, accessory structure, or other structure, having four enclosing walls and a roof, built according to and in compliance with all applicable building, zoning, fire, or other codes of the city. 
    Automobile graveyard means any establishment or place of business which is duly licensed and operated in accordance with all applicable laws and/or ordinances of the city, and which is maintained, used, or operated for storing, keeping, buying, or selling of wrecked, ruined, damaged, or dismantled motor vehicles or parts thereof. 
    Commercial property means any lot, tract, parcel, land, or other property located within the city that is zoned or designated for uses other than residential purposes. 
    Garbage means the animal and/or vegetable putrescible waste resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking or consumption of food or food products. 
    Improved subdivision means a division of a tract of land or acreage into tracts or parcels, and the improvement thereof by construction of streets, water lines and, where applicable, sewer lines to serve the subdivided property. 
    Inoperable means incapable of being used for the manufactured, designed or intended purpose. 
    Inoperable vehicle means any vehicle not currently licensed; in a state of disassembly; in the process of being stripped, dismantled, or overhauled; or undergoing body work; or any other condition that renders the vehicle inoperable or incapable of being used for its designed or intended purpose. 
    Junk means and includes all metals, whether ferrous or nonferrous, including, but not limited to, any used or secondhand parts of machinery; plumbing fixtures, or parts thereof; parts of an automobile, truck, bus, motorcycle, water craft, or other motor vehicle; gas or electrical appliances or fixtures, or parts thereof; household hardware; wire; cable; bearings; valves; pipes and pipe-fittings; building materials; wood; or any other used or secondhand metal articles, including inoperable motor vehicles. 
    Junk or salvage yard means any premises, establishment, or place of business which is duly licensed and operated in accordance with all applicable laws and/or ordinances of the city, and which is maintained, operated, or used for storing, keeping, or dismantling of junk and salvage, but shall not include the place of business or premises of a scrap processor as herein defined. 
    Litter means all waste material which can be or is subject to being blown from place to place or scattered by the elements, including, but not limited to, paper; cardboard; cartons; boxes; plastics; rags; cloth; fibers and fabrics; leather; polyethylene; and polystyrenes. 
    Natural condition means uncultivated and unseeded land, still in a state of nature. But any growth on land once it has been cleared or plowed is not a natural condition, even though it has not been planted or cultivated by anyone. 
    Owner of property means the title holder or person having right of possession of real property and includes legal title holder as shown of record in the tax assessor's office, or agent of legal title holder of said property. 
    Premises means any lot, yard, plot, tract, parcel, or other piece of land or property located within the city. 
    Residential property means any lot, tract, parcel, land, or other property located within the city, on which single or multifamily structures used as a residence or for human habitation exists, or any property that is located within an area that is zoned for residential uses by the city. 
    Scrap means other materials or waste, including, but not limited to, old cordage, ropes; rubber; bottles and other glass; tin or aluminum cans; buckets; tree branches, tree limbs, tree stumps; or other waste or refuse not otherwise classified herein as junk, litter, or garbage. 
    Scrap metal yard means any establishment or place of business which is duly licensed and operated in accordance with all applicable laws and/or ordinances of the city, state, and which is maintained, used, or operated solely for the processing or preparing of scrap metals for re-melting by steel mills and foundries. 
    Scrap processor means any person who is duly licensed and operating in accordance with all applicable laws and/or ordinances of the city, and is engaged primarily in the purchase and collection of scrap metals (e.g. manufacturing byproducts, obsolescent machinery, and vehicles) for the specific purpose of processing into scrap materials for the metals recovery industry, such as steel mills, foundries, smelters, and refineries, and having machinery and facilities designed for such processing, and making regular shipments of such materials in the normal course of business. 
    Vehicle means any device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported, carried, or drawn from one place to another, and shall include, but not be limited to, motor vehicles, boat trailers, utility trailers, horse trailers, bicycles, carts, tractors, or other devices. 
    Weed nuisance means any abundance of overgrown weeds or grass within the city, which is injurious to the general public health, safety and general welfare by providing breeding grounds and shelter for rats, mice, snakes, mosquitoes and other vermin, insects and pests; or attaining such heights and dryness so as to constitute a serious fire threat or hazard; or bearing winged or downy seeds, when mature, that cause the spread of weeds and, when breathed, irritation to the throat, lungs and eyes of the public; or hiding debris, such as broken glass or metal, which could inflict injury on any person going upon the property; or being unsightly; or any growth of weeds, other than ornamental plant growth, which exceeds 12 inches in height. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful and constitute a nuisance for the owner of any real property situated within the city to allow such real property to become overgrown with weeds or grass so as to constitute a weed nuisance as defined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(c)  It shall be the duty of the owner of any real property located within the city to maintain any weeds growing upon said property in such a manner as not to constitute a weed nuisance as defined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(d)  This section shall not apply to the following: 
(1)  Any property which is in its natural condition. 
(2)  Any property which is located outside any improved subdivision and is located more than 100 feet from any boundary of any lot; or parcel of real estate upon which any dwelling is located, and more than 100 feet from any commercial enterprise. 
(3)  Cultivated row crops and garden plants in their respective growing seasons. This exception applies only to growing crops and garden plants, and shall not be construed to permit any crops or gardens to become overgrown with weeds in violation of the remaining terms of this section. 
(4)  Ornamental shrubbery and ground cover, provided that such uses are part of a landscaping theme and not associated with a general deterioration of the property. 
(e)  All weed nuisances may be declared to be a public nuisance by the governing body of the city and thereafter abated at the cost of the owner as provided in Code of Ala. 1975, title 11, ch. 67, art. 5 (Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-67-80 et seq.), using the procedures provided therein. 
(f)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section for any person to store or keep upon the premises of any residential or commercial property, within the city, any inoperable vehicle, scrap, or junk, as defined in subsection (a) of this section, unless the same is housed in an approved, enclosed, covered structure. This subsection shall not apply to the following: 
(1)  Materials stored or located on the premises of any junk or salvage yard, scrap metal yard, scrap processor, or automobile graveyard, as defined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(2)  Vehicles being repaired or awaiting repair that are located on the premises of any automobile dealer, automobile repair and body shop or garage, or other vehicle repair enterprise that is duly licensed and operated in compliance with all applicable codes and ordinances of the city, provided said vehicles are so located or stored in a manner as to prevent any health, fire, or safety hazard. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section to keep or store upon the premises of any retail store or shop, secondhand store, thrift store, or similar commercial property or establishment, any merchandise, goods, or wares, including, but not limited to, gas or electric appliances, or parts thereof; plumbing fixtures, or parts thereof; lawn mowers or lawn mower parts; machinery, equipment, utensils, or other items displayed for sale to the general public, in such a manner as to constitute a health, safety, or fire hazard. 
(h)  It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section for any person in charge of any residential or commercial property to fail to maintain the property free from litter and garbage as defined in subsection (a) of this section, unless said litter and garbage is containerized and stored in such a manner as to prevent it from being blown, deposited, or otherwise scattered by the elements, animals, birds, or any other means. 
(i)  It shall be the duty of the owner, or any person in control of or charge of property located within the city, to maintain said property in compliance with the provisions of this section, free of any inoperable vehicles, scrap, junk, garbage, or litter as defined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Ord. No. 356, § 1, 4-26-1993) 
Secs. 30-2-30-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CITY COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 30-21. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Garbage and trash means and includes all waste and discarded materials including rubbish and debris, waste and discarded food, animal and vegetable matter, but not including liquid waste, waste paper cans, glass, crockery, rags, ashes, cinders, brush, grass, weeds, cuttings from lawns and gardens; when such substances are placed in a garbage container as herein defined. 
    Garbage and trash dump means the place for dumping and disposing of garbage and trash, operated by the city or by others as may be contracted for by said city. 
    Garbage container means and includes a water-tight receptacle or can having a capacity of not more than 30 gallons, of substantial metal construction, with a tight-fitting lid or cover, and two handles on the sides of the receptacle or can, or with a bail by which same can be conveniently lifted or moved. 
    Person means and includes a natural person, firm, association, partnership, corporation, trustee, executor, administrator or legal entity, whether singular or plural, masculine or feminine, as the context may require. 
(Ord. No. 280, § I, 4-9-1956) 
Sec. 30-22. - Use mandatory; rates. 
(a)  Use of the garbage and trash collection, hauling and disposal service (garbage service) operated by the city is hereby required and made mandatory for: 
(1)  Each residence (one family); 
(2)  Residences (multifamily) and apartment houses, each unit or family; 
(3)  Each trailer (if situated on trailer court premises, this charge is payable by the owner or operator of the trailer court for each trailer situated thereon); 
(4)  Each business which is situated within the corporate limits, and the charges for such garbage service shall be paid to the city each month by each such user according to the applicable base rate monthly charges as are in effect for such user for such service. 
(b)  The garbage and trash collection, hauling and disposal service operated by the city, heretofore provided for in 1956 by the city's municipal garbage disposal ordinance, shall be continued. The collection, hauling and disposal of garbage and trash shall be made by the officers, agents and employees of the city under the direction of the mayor. The charges herein prescribed for such service are based upon the service being made available to residences and trailer courts once a day, twice a week and to businesses once a day from Monday through Saturday of each week. In cases requiring collection and disposal at more frequent intervals, an additional charge to the hereinafter set forth base rate shall also be imposed, and this additional charge shall be calculated by multiplying the base rate by the fractional proportion of the number of regular pick-ups as are represented by the additional pick-ups required. Beginning with the month of July, 1971, and continuing each succeeding month thereafter, the following base rate monthly charges are hereby imposed by the city for the collecting, hauling and disposing of garbage, to-wit: 
(1)  The monthly charges imposed by the city for collecting, handling and disposing of garbage for business or commercial establishments shall be as established from time to time by the city. 
(2)  The monthly charges imposed by the city for the collecting, handling and disposing of garbage for residences shall be as established from time to time by the city. Any person whose sole income or means of support is a Social Security payment shall be exempt from the payment of residential garbage fees. 
(3)  Any exemption under this article shall not attach until applied for by the person claiming said exemption, an investigation into the information provided by the applicant and approval by the clerk. 
(4)  All bills for garbage service shall be due and payable monthly. The waterworks, sewer and gas board of the city is designated as the city's agent for the collection of such charges and shall remit to the city periodically as such charges are collected. In the case of utility customers of the board, such charges shall be designated on the utilities bill and the same shall be due and payable to the board at the same time the bill for utility services is due. Other persons liable for the garbage service charges who are not utility customers of the board shall also be billed monthly by the board, and such billing shall show a due date thereon which is the same dated as would be shown as the due date if such billing was for utility services of the board, and such garbage service charges shall be due and payable to the board by the due date shown on the bill. 
(5)  Any person, firm or corporation who fails to make timely payment of the garbage service charges provided for in the city municipal garbage disposal ordinance, as amended, or who violates any of the other provisions of this article, as amended, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. No. 280, § II, 4-9-1956; Ord. No. 93, § 1, 6-14-1971; Ord. No. 152, § 1, 11-22-1976; Ord. No. 169, § 1, 1-23-1978; Ord. No. 184, § 1, 2-26-1979; Ord. No. 254, § 1, 11-10-1986; Ord. No. 309, § 1, 7-9-1990; Ord. No. 315, § 1, 22-5-1990; Ord. No. 347, § 1, 12-14-1992; Ord. No. 350, § 1, 1-25-1993; Ord. No. 477, § 1, 4-7-2003) 
Sec. 30-23. - Placement of certain materials for collection. 
    Boxes, crates, grass, leaves, tree trimmings and shrubbery cuttings not more than five feet in length nor weighing over 50 pounds and originating on the premises from which the street department removes garbage and trash for a service charge as provided in this article shall be placed in front of such premises on the area between the sidewalk and street on the regular collection days for removal by the street department without additional charges therefor; provided, however, not more than one truck load shall be removed without charges on any one collection day. 
(Ord. No. 280, § III, 4-9-1956) 
Sec. 30-24. - Collection agreement. 
(a)  Any person, firm or corporation desiring use of the garbage service provided in this article shall enter into agreement with the city words and figures substantially as follows: 
    "The undersigned desires the use of the garbage service provided by the City of Scottsboro, and agrees to pay therefor, the sum of $ ____________ for a month ____________ , payable each month when and as the bill for utility service is paid, the same to be billed with each utility bill; and in the event the same is not paid when and as such utility bill is paid, then the City of Scottsboro, may discontinue the garbage service. 
    The same may be reinstated upon the same conditions such utility service is reinstated. 
    Witness my hand this ____________ day of ____________ 20 ____________ 
    ____________ " 
(b)  If no utility service is being furnished, then the person desiring such service shall enter into agreement with the city for such service and pay therefor in advance. 
(Ord. No. 280, § V, 4-9-1956) 
Sec. 30-25. - No service to delinquent accounts. 
    No garbage collection service shall be rendered by the street department for any person, firm or corporation whose account for said service is delinquent by more than 15 days. 
(Ord. No. 280, § VI, 4-9-1956) 
Sec. 30-26. - Nuisances. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to allow garbage or trash to remain exposed to flies on their premises. 
(Ord. No. 280, § VII, 4-9-1956) 
Secs. 30-27-30-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LANDFILL AND CITY BALER 

Sec. 30-56. - Fees and charges established. 
    The city fees and charges, which shall be paid to the city by persons and firms disposing of garbage and trash at either the city's sanitary landfill or at the city's garbage and trash baler, shall be as established from time to time by the city. 
(Ord. No. 183, § 1, 2-26-1979) 
Sec. 30-57. - Limitations. 
    Such use of the city's landfill and garbage and trash baler, for which fees and charges are herein established, shall be limited to residents of and businesses located in the city. 
(Ord. No. 183, § 1, 2-26-1979) 
Secs. 30-58-30-87. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - TRASH AND OTHER MATERIAL PICK-UP 

Sec. 30-88. - Fees. 
    With respect to waste such as stumps, tree tops, limbs and brush resulting from site clearing and other land clearing activities, waste from the demolishment of or repair of buildings, construction waste, and other matters not included in the regular routine trash pick-ups, the city street department on behalf of the city shall impose and collect a special charge as established from time to time by the city. Any contractor in charge of the operation generating or producing these wastes, or the owner of such premises in question if there is no such contractor, is charged with the duty and responsibility of: 
(1)  Notifying the city through its street department immediately as soon as there is an accumulation of more than one truck load of such waste; and 
(2)  Making arrangement and timely payment to the city of the special charge hereby imposed at the time said charge is incurred or by executing and delivering to the city an appropriate written obligation promising to pay within ten days said special charge owed pursuant to this division. The city street department shall remove these wastes as expeditiously as possible and avoid the accumulation of these wastes as is reasonably practicable. 
(Ord. No. 322, § 1, 5-13-1991; Ord. No. 525, § 1, 7-23-2007) 
Sec. 30-89. - Trees and tree limbs. 
    Any person clearing lots or building sites shall cut trees and limbs in lengths of no more than ten feet each and shall place or stack the same in an orderly manner on or near the street right-of-way so as to be accessible for city street department pick-up, and the tree stumps and other debris incident to such clearing operations shall be placed in separate piles from the trees and limbs on or near the street right-of-way so as to be accessible for city street department pick-up. 
(Ord. No. 322, § 2, 5-13-1991) 
Sec. 30-90. - Demolition or repair wastes. 
    All wastes from the demolishment or repair of buildings and all construction wastes shall be broken down into such sizes and weights as to be accessible for city street department pick-up by the city street department equipment and personnel available for such purposes without the necessity of additional manpower or equipment to handle or load the same. 
(Ord. No. 322, § 3, 5-13-1991) 
Sec. 30-91. - Placement restrictions. 
    None of the wastes referred to in sections 30-88 through 30-90, and no grass or brush, whether or not resulting from clearing operations, shall be placed for pick-up in any gutter or on any sidewalk or any traveled portion of any public street in the city. 
(Ord. No. 322, § 4, 5-13-1991) 
Chapter 32 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES 

Sec. 32-1. - Pavement cutting. 
(a)  A $20.00 fee per lane of highway or street will be required for a permit, to be obtained from the city, at the city hall or at the office of the city waterworks, sewer, and gas board prior to any cutting, trenching, disturbing, or removing any portion of existing pavement or asphalt covered street or parking lot maintained by the city or in the boundaries of the city limits. 
(b)  All pavement cuts or trench cuts shall be made in a neat straight line cut in pavement to be made with a paving breaker or an equivalent type tool so as not to tear or rip up excessive pavement. 
(c)  All excavated materials from ditches or trenches shall be hauled off or disposed of and backfilled with crusher run type stone or washed stone and compacted to the grade of the existing pavement. 
(d)  The contractor will be responsible to keep ditches or trenches filled and graded to sufficiently accommodate flow of traffic without hazardous holes or drop-offs in the street until city maintenance crews can re-pave or patch said crossing. 
(e)  The contractor shall have proper barricades or warning signs for any street work or construction and be responsible for same until such time for city crews to re-pave or patch any removed pavement. 
(f)  The contractor shall be responsible for any damage to city utilities, sidewalks, curbs and gutters or damage to any city property not covered on original permit issued. Extent of damage or extra cost for same will be determined by authorized city officials. 
(g)  Any ditch or trench cut exceeding a width of 24 inches and/or running length-wise or angling across street, will require a special permit from authorized city officials to determine extra costs accordingly. 
(Ord. No. 200, § I, 2-23-1981) 
Sec. 32-2. - Obstructions. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to encumber, block or obstruct a public street or a public sidewalk in the city with a fence, a chain, a gate, or other means. 
(Ord. No. 251, § 1, 4-14-1986) 
Sec. 32-3. - Public utility access. 
(a)  Where a public utility facility has existed over; under, along or across any property in the city limits of the city for a period of seven years or more, or was so placed with the property owners' knowledge and consent, the public utility shall have a right of ingress and egress to such facility of sufficient length, width and depth to operate and maintain safe and reliable service. A facility built, operated, or maintained by a public utility for the sole benefit of the property owner shall not be subject to this subsection. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to erect or maintain buildings or other structures or objects or to store materials, either temporarily or permanently, in a manner which might endanger the facilities of a public utility of the city, or endanger the general public, or prevent access to or maintenance of these facilities by such public utility or the city or its or their agents, employees, equipment or vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 247, § § 2, 3, 10-28-1985) 
Chapter 34 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Motor vehicles and traffic, Code of Ala. 1975, title 32. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 34-1. - Traffic signs, signals, etc. 
    The location and existence of all traffic control signs, signals, devices and markings are ratified and confirmed. 
Sec. 34-2. - Seizure and forfeiture of automobiles where operators unable to produce valid driver's license on demand of law enforcement officer. 
(a)  The city council finds and declares all of the following: 
(1)  Driving a motor vehicle on the public streets and highways is a privilege, not a right. 
(2)  Of all drivers involved in fatal accidents, a driver with a suspended license is more likely to be involved in a fatal accident than a properly licensed driver. 
(3)  Alabamians who comply with the law are frequently victims of traffic accidents caused by unlicensed drivers. These innocent victims suffer considerable pain and property loss at the hands of people who flaunt the law. 
(4)  It is necessary and appropriate to take additional steps to prevent unlicensed drivers from driving. The city has a critical interest in enforcing its traffic laws and in keeping unlicensed drivers from illegally driving. Seizing the motor vehicles used by unlicensed drivers serves a significant governmental and public interest, namely the protection of the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of the city from the harm of unlicensed drivers who are involved in a disproportionate number of traffic incidents, and the avoidance of the associated destruction and damage to lives and property. 
(5)  This section is consistent with the due process requirements of the United States Constitution and the holding of the Supreme Court of the United States in Calera-Toledo v. Pearson Yacht Leasing Co., 416 U.S. 663, 94 S. Ct. 2080, 40 L. Ed. 2d 452 (1974). 
(b)  A driver unable to produce a valid driver's license shall be subject to the following provisions: 
(1)  Towing a vehicle when a driver is unable to produce a valid driver's license. 
a.  If a driver is unable to produce a valid driver's license on the demand of a law enforcement officer, the motor vehicle is subject to impoundment regardless of ownership, unless the law enforcement officer is reasonably able, by other means, to verify that the driver is properly licensed. Prior to impounding the motor vehicle, a law enforcement officer shall make a reasonable attempt to verify the license status of a driver who claims to be properly licensed, but who is unable to produce the license on demand of the law enforcement officer. A notation of the officer's attempt to verify that the driver is properly licensed shall be noted on the departmental report. The driver and occupants of the motor vehicle will be transported to a place of safety by the impounding officer and a vehicle impound report made with a full inventory of items in the motor vehicle. 
b.  A law enforcement officer shall not impound a motor vehicle pursuant to this section if the license of the driver expired within the preceding 60 days and the driver would otherwise have been properly licensed. 
c.  If the owner of the motor vehicle or another family member of the owner is present in the motor vehicle and has a valid license, the motor vehicle shall not be impounded and towed. 
d.  If there is a medical necessity jeopardizing life or limb, the law enforcement officer may elect not to impound the motor vehicle. 
e.  A law enforcement officer who requests that a motor vehicle be towed onto the property of another pursuant to this section shall do so by using a vehicle impound report. 
(2)  A motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this section shall be released if the person redeeming the motor vehicle satisfies in full the fees provided for by subsection (d) of this section and: 
a.  The registered owner appears at the police department, or a representative of the owner with written notarized authorization from the registered owner appears, and presents a valid driver's license and a copy of the written authorization, if applicable, to be copied by the police department; 
b.  If the registered owner does not have a valid driver's license, he may bring someone with him who has a verified valid license and the motor vehicle may be released without written notarized permission; or 
c.  Upon order of a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(c)  Any owner of a motor vehicle (including a lienholder, person with a security interest in the motor vehicle, a lessor of the motor vehicle, assignee of the lessor, or the person who is the registered owner of the motor vehicle) who suffers any loss due to the impoundment of any motor vehicle pursuant to this section may recover the amount of the loss from the driver who was unable to produce a valid driver's license at the request of the law enforcement officer. 
(d)  The person redeeming the motor vehicle from the automobile dealer, wrecker service owner, repair service owner, or person, firm, or governmental entity on whose property the motor vehicle was lawfully towed at the written request of a law enforcement officer pursuant to this section will be responsible for paying the set fee for the removal and for the storage of the motor vehicle. 
(e)  If a motor vehicle impounded pursuant to this section is not redeemed or claimed pursuant to this section within 60 days of the date that it is impounded, then the automobile dealer, wrecker service or repair service owner, or any person, firm, or governmental entity on whose property the motor vehicle was lawfully towed at the written request of a law enforcement officer pursuant to this section may sell the motor vehicle at public auction according to the state law governing abandoned motor vehicles in Code of Ala. 1975, §§ 32-13-1-32-13-8. 
(Ord. No. 532, § 1, 1-14-2008) 
State Law reference- Impoundment of motor vehicles driven by unlicensed persons, Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-6-19. 
Sec. 34-3. - Distracted driving. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful and constitute an offense against the city for any person to drive a motor vehicle recklessly or heedlessly while distracted or in willful, wanton, reckless or negligent disregard for the rights or safety of persons or property, or without due caution and circumspection so as to endanger or be likely to endanger any person or property. 
(b)  Driving while distracted may be considered by the courts of the city to be a lesser included offense under a charge of reckless driving. 
(c)  This section shall not apply to vehicles operated by licensed police officers, firefighters, ambulance drivers, and other public safety employees in performance of emergency duties. 
(Ord. No. 564, §§ 1, 3, 4, 1-18-2011) 
Sec. 34-4. - Cutting corners to avoid traffic devices. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or drive any motor vehicle upon the streets or highways of the city, or within the police jurisdiction thereof, at any intersection where gasoline filling stations or other business property is located, so as to cause such vehicle to cut the corners of any such intersection by passing over the space used in the operation of such filling station or other business property, and thereby avoid the traffic light or traffic signal at any such intersection, or so as to avoid stopping at any such intersection as is required by the laws of the city, or so as to avoid traveling at any such intersection over the usual lanes of traffic. 
(Ord. No. 131, § 1, 11-24-1975) 
Secs. 34-5-34-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 34-23. - Towing illegally parked vehicles. 
    Any vehicle parked upon a public street at a place, in a manner, or for a length of time prohibited by any ordinance of the city including this article, now in effect or which may be hereafter adopted, is, if such vehicle is unattended, hereby declared to be an obstruction in such street and a public nuisance, and any police officer of the city is hereby authorized to remove the same, or cause the same to be removed, to the depository provided by the city for such purposes and impounded therein. 
(Ord. No. 12, § 3, 2-10-1958) 
Sec. 34-24. - Towing vehicles parked for 48 hours. 
    Any unattended vehicle parked upon the public streets of the city, though not parked in violation of an ordinance of the city, may, if such unattended vehicle remains parked at such place for as long as 48 hours after the owner or proprietor of the property adjacent or contiguous to that portion of the street where such vehicle is parked has submitted a signed, written request to the mayor that such vehicle be removed, be deemed an obstruction in such street and is hereby declared to be a public nuisance, and any police officer of the city is hereby authorized to remove the same, or cause the same to be removed, to the depository provided by the city for such purpose, and impounded therein. 
(Ord. No. 12, § 4, 2-10-1958) 
Sec. 34-25. - Redemption of impounded vehicles. 
    When any vehicle has been impounded by the city according to the provisions of section 34-23 or 34-24 the owner of the same, upon proper proof of ownership made to the mayor or chief of police of the city, and upon payment to the city of a towing and impounding fee as provided in Ordinance Number 579 shall be allowed to redeem such vehicle so removed and impounded by the city. 
(Ord. No. 12, § 5, 2-10-1958) 
Sec. 34-26. - Parking zones generally. 
(a)  Unless the context clearly indicates a different meaning, the following words, whenever used in this article, shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them in this section. 
    Vehicle means every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a public highway, excepting devices moved by human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
(b)  Subject to the approval of the mayor and council of the city shall have the duty to direct and authorize and mark off "No Parking" zones or areas as he designates a traffic hazard or dangerous congested area. 
(c)  When signs are erected on any street or part of street giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle on the side or sides of any such street or part of street so designated for no parking. 
(Ord. No. 155, §§ 1-3, 12-28-1976) 
Sec. 34-27. - Fire lanes, emergency lanes, etc. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Emergency lane/fire lane means a part of a public access area, as defined herein, which is designed to provide clear and unobstructed access to emergency vehicles, equipment, and personnel to and from all 30,000 square feet and above mercantile occupancies adjacent to or serviced by such public access area. Emergency lanes shall be a minimum of 60 feet in length and eight feet in width and shall be located in front of, or adjacent to, each public entrance to such occupancies and structures. 
    Public access areas means any publically owned property or any privately owned property provided for the general public for the movement or parking of vehicles in connection with a shopping center or publically owned structures used for assembly or educational purposes. 
(b)  No parking shall be permitted at any time on any emergency lane or marked fire lane, and no parking shall be permitted at any location which would prevent access to any emergency lane, or fire hydrant, by any emergency response equipment. 
(c)  No person shall stop, let stand, or park a vehicle whether occupied or not, in any emergency lane or fire lane at any time, and no owner, manager, or tenant of any premises shall permit any customer or visitor to stop, let stand, or park any vehicle on any part of any of any emergency lane or fire lane at any time. Notwithstanding the foregoing, a person may stop a vehicle temporarily in an emergency lane for the limited purposes of allowing passengers in the vehicle to disembark or allowing persons waiting on the vehicle to board. 
(d)  The property owner of any property such to the emergency lane/fire lane requirements of this section shall mark each emergency lane with red paint curbs or, where curbs are absent, with a red painted six-inch-wide lane line along the entire length of the emergency or fire lane to warn people against the blocking of the lane.
