The owner of the area where an emergency or fire lane is located shall also post appropriate signs indicating that the emergency or fire lane is an emergency or fire lane and indicating that no parking is permitted in the emergency or fire lane. The owner shall erect one such sign for every 50 feet of distance along the curb adjacent to the emergency lane or fire lane or, where curbs are absent, adjacent to the red painted lane line. Each sign shall be maintained in a good state of repair by the property owner. 
(e)  The owner of an area of property where a stand pipe or sprinkler system connection is located shall post appropriate signs indicating that no parking is permitted in that zone. Any person, firm, or corporation who shall receive said citation shall be fined $25.00 if said citation is paid within a 48-hour period. 
(f)  Any person, firm, or corporation receiving a citation and not paying the said $25.00 fine within 48 hours shall be subject to arrest and upon conviction shall be fined not less than $100.00. 
(Ord. No. 398, §§ 1-4, 6, 7, 10-23-1995) 
Secs. 34-28-34-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - TWO-HOUR PARKING 

Sec. 34-56. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Vehicle means any device by which any person or property may be transported on streets or highways. 
(Ord. No. 173, § 1, 7-24-1978) 
Sec. 34-57. - Zones. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle on a public street or highway within the city which has been designated as limited parking for a period of longer than two hours; such designation to be shown by appropriate signs. 
(Ord. No. 173, § 2, 7-24-1978) 
Sec. 34-58. - Citation forms. 
    The chief of police is hereby directed to supply police officers with citations for the purpose of giving notices to persons in violation of any portion of this division and shall also provide police officers with the necessary implements for proper tire marking in order to properly enforce this division. 
(Ord. No. 173, § 3, 7-24-1978) 
Sec. 34-59. - Days and hours applicable. 
    The provisions of this division shall apply every day after adoption and publication of the ordinance from which this division is derived between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. except Sundays and holidays and provided further that, within the meaning of this division, the term "holiday" shall include the following days only, January 1, July 4, the first Monday in September, December 25, and the day designated and set aside by the President of the United States as a day of Thanksgiving. With the exception of each first Monday of each month, on this such day the area described as Jackson County Courthouse Square means the public parking area and public ways or streets surrounding the county courthouse grounds and Laurel Street on the north, Market Street on the east, Peachtree Street on the south, and Broad Street on the west. The designated parallel parking on Laurel Street, Peachtree Street, Market Street and Broad Street, surrounding the Courthouse Square shall be exempt from the two-hour parking limit after the purchase on a First Monday Trade Day permit. 
(Ord. No. 173, § 4, 7-24-1978) 
Sec. 34-60. - Citation fine. 
    Any person, firm, or corporation who shall receive said citation shall be fined $5.00 if said citation is paid within a 48-hour period. 
(Ord. No. 173, § 5, 7-24-1978; Ord. No. 397, § 1, 10-23-1995) 
Sec. 34-61. - Failure to pay fine. 
    Any person, firm or corporation receiving a citation and not paying the said $5.00 fine within 48 hours will be subject to arrest and upon conviction shall be fined not less than $10.00 and not more than $50.00. 
(Ord. No. 176, § 1, 7-24-1978; Ord. No. 397, § 1, 10-23-1995) 
Secs. 34-62-34-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - WRECKERS/TOWING SERVICE 

Sec. 34-81. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the same meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Applicant means the operator of a wrecker or tow service who, after being advised of the requirements and regulations for participation therein, makes known his desire to voluntarily participate in the city's rotation roster by making application for the same. 
    Chief of police means the chief of the city's police department or his designee. 
    Contract wrecker/tow service means that wrecker company which has contracted with the city to provide wrecker services requested by the city, for public safety reasons, as opposed to wrecker services requested by a private individual. 
    Department means the city police department. 
    Fire department emergency incident commander means the highest-ranking fire department official who is in charge of the hazardous material incidents and other emergency situations which may arise while executing the mission of the fire department. Duties include, but are not limited to the following: 
    Management decisions means decisions related to personnel, equipment, procedures, etc., at the scene of any emergency incident. 
    Fire extinguisher means a portable device used for extinguishing fires as defined by the National Board of Fire Underwriters, dry chemical extinguisher with either a 5 or 10 B.C. rating and in a quick-release carrier which is capable of extinguishing fires. 
    Impoundment means a seizure of a vehicle made by legal process by the city police department. 
    Large wreckers means and shall be classified as any of the following types of wreckers or tow trucks, tandem dual wheel or tandem rear end wreckers, or twin booms with factory rated or tested lifting capacity of 12 5/10 tons or over per drum and per winch and per winch line, with dual drum capacity, hydraulic or power take-off driven, and shall be equipped with dual rear twin-screw axles, and shall be equipped with quick air couplings for towing vehicles with air brakes, and shall be utilized to tow any vehicle having a gross weight exceeding 10,000 pounds, or any vehicle having dual rear axles or any tractor-trailer combination. The wrecker company shall provide documentation of lifting capacity from the manufacturer or qualified testing facility. 
    Motor vehicle means every vehicle which is self-propelled. 
    Owner means any person who holds a legal title to a motor vehicle or who has the legal right of possession thereof. 
    Place of business means the place where the wrecker or tow truck company conducts business and is licensed pursuant to municipal law. 
    Police officer means any duly sworn law enforcement officer employed by the city. 
    Repossessor means any person in the business of providing repossession services to others or who performs repossession services on its own behalf, and includes, but is not limited to, officers, managers, agents or employees thereof. 
    Repossession wrecker or tow truck means any wrecker or tow truck, or large wrecker or tow truck, as defined herein, used for the sole purpose of repossessing vehicles. The term "repossession wrecker" shall include vehicles that are commonly referred to as "snatch trucks," as well as any and all motor vehicles used to tow or remove any vehicle from one location to another. Repossession wreckers shall not apply to wreckers or tow trucks used for the dual purpose of performing regular wrecker services and repossession services. 
    Rotation roster means the rotation list of wreckers or tow truck companies available for request by private individuals as prepared and used as provided in the execution of this rule and regulation policy. The city accident and impoundment rotation roster shall be considered and defined as a privilege and not a right. 
    Street means a thoroughfare, including public streets, lanes, alleys, etc., within the city and its police jurisdiction which is reserved for vehicle traffic. 
    Traffic hazard means any disabled vehicle, other than those resulting from a vehicular accident as defined herein, and which is an obstruction to the normal flow or movement of vehicle and pedestrian traffic on any public street within the jurisdiction of the city. 
    Vehicle means every device in or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a public street, except devices moved only by human power, or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks, and shall include trailers and semi-trailers. 
    Vehicular accident means any incident involving contact between a vehicle and any other object or vehicle which results in disabling damage to any vehicle requiring the services of a wrecker or tow truck. 
    Wrecker means any motor vehicle used for the purpose of towing or removing motor vehicles from one location to another location, for any purpose. 
    Wrecker or towing business means the act of towing or removing motor vehicles from one location to another location, for any reason, where either the beginning or ending location is within the city. This definition shall not include situations whereby a business owns or leases wreckers for the sole purpose of towing other vehicles owned or leased by the business. 
    Wrecker company means any person engaged in the wrecker or tow business. 
    Wrecker operator means any person who drives or otherwise uses a wrecker for a wrecker business as defined herein. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 1, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-82. - Vehicle and equipment inspection and requirements. 
    Each wrecker company participating in the city's wrecker rotation program shall be inspected by the city police department at least once per year and more often if indications arise that the wrecker company is not in compliance with the following provisions: Equipment and certification prerequisite for all wreckers: 
(1)  All equipment necessary for the towing vehicle or the combination of the towing vehicle and towed vehicle must comply with the applicable requirements of 49 CFR 390-399 of the Federal Motor Carrier Rules and Regulations, as they currently exist or as they may be amended in the future. Any future amendments of the Federal Motor Carrier Rules and Regulations which result in a conflict with the additional requirements contained in this section shall be resolved in favor of compliance with the Federal Motor Carrier Rules and Regulations. 
(2)  In the interest of safe and operational equipment and the public's safety, no application will be processed without the applicant first submitting a certified copy of the state wrecker inspection checklist. The applicant wrecker company must be a member or participant of, and in compliance with, the department of public safety (Huntsville Trooper Post) accident wrecker rotation program. Prior to be being placed on the wrecker rotation roster, the applicant shall present and make available for inspection by the chief of police or his designee all wreckers, business facilities and equipment that are to be used by the applicant for the provision of wrecker services. 
(3)  Following inspection and assurances of certifications by the city police department, each wrecker shall be issued a decal which shall be displayed in the lower left corner of the wrecker or tow truck's windshield. Each decal shall indicate the wrecker permit number and the current calendar year. The fee for each annual inspection and issuance of each annual inspection decal shall be a fee of $15.00 payable to the city police department. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 2, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-83. - Reports of repossession required. 
(a)  Every wrecker company or repossessor who repossesses a motor vehicle within the city limits shall notify the city police department records division by providing information on the vehicle repossessed, where, type of vehicle, time of repossession and which company, within one hour after the repossession has been completed and shall also file a written incident report of the repossession at least 48 hours after the repossession is completed. 
(b)  At the time of the repossession, every wrecker company operator or repossessor who repossess a motor vehicle within the city limits shall be required to have official paperwork authorizing the repossession of the vehicle on his person. The authorizing paperwork shall include, at minimum, the name of the authorizing authority, the name of the person or entity believed to be in possession of the vehicle, and a description of the vehicle to include license plate number and vehicle identification number. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 3, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-84. - Applications and conditions for participation in wrecker rotation program. 
(a)  Written requests for participation in the wrecker rotation system or program. Each applicant desiring to be placed on the rotation roster shall file a written application with the police chief or his designee on a form furnished by the city police department. A new applicant may file a written application at any time. Once an applicant has be accepted and placed on the rotation roster, applications for renewal shall be submitted in January of each year thereafter, and shall adhere to all of the same terms and conditions as apply to new applicants. The city accident and impoundment rotation roster shall be considered and defined as a privilege and not a right. An applicant may request to discontinue participation in the rotation roster at any time. 
(b)  Equipment certification. Each applicant shall certify that each wrecker to be utilized in service of the rotation roster meets or exceeds the following requirements at the time the application is made: 
(1)  For each regular haul wrecker, in addition to the criteria established in section 34-82, a conventional wrecker must be equipped with dollies and wheel lifts or hydraulic operated tilting bed trucks, with a one-ton rated chassis or larger and equipped with a broom and shovel, two fully charged rated fire extinguishers, and agents to remove oil spills from the roadway. 
(2)  The name of the company must be permanently affixed on each side of the wrecker in four-inch-high or larger letters and the address and telephone number in two-inch-high or larger letters or numerals. 
(3)  All safety equipment, horns, lights, flashers, amber lights, brakes and other similar equipment must be operational. 
(4)  In the interest of safe and operational equipment and the public's safety, no application will be processed without first submitting a certified copy of the state wrecker inspection checklist. The applicant wrecker company must be a member or participant of, and in compliance with, the department of public safety (Huntsville Trooper Post) accident wrecker rotation program. 
(c)  Copy of rules and regulations. The chief of police or his designee will furnish each applicant with a copy of the rules and regulations pertaining to the operation of wreckers within the wrecker rotation system. 
(d)  Business license required. Prior to being placed on the wrecker rotation roster, the applicant must furnish the chief of police or his designee with a copy of a current, valid business license issued by the city in the applicant's name. 
(e)  Storage facilities. Prior to being placed on the wrecker rotation roster, the applicant must agree to a preapproval inspection of the wrecker company's premises to ensure adequate outside storage sufficient to accommodate a minimum of ten vehicles, which is well and continuously lighted during the hours of darkness and, at minimum, include an area completely enclosed within a six-foot-high chain link or other equivalent fencing material designed to protect against unauthorized entry. Any inside storage must be within a supervised or locked building. In addition to the provision of a secure storage area, each wrecker company shall employ reasonable safeguards and procedures so that all personal belongings and contents in a stored vehicle remain intact and are returned to the vehicle's owner or agent upon request or upon release of the vehicle. 
(f)  Location of storage facility. The wrecker company, wreckers utilized, operators, and storage facilities must be located within the city limits. 
(g)  Certificate of insurance. The wrecker company participating on the wrecker rotation roster, from the time he moves or otherwise makes contact with any vehicle to be towed, assumes liability for injury to persons, damage to property, fires, or theft resulting from the operators negligent acts or omissions. Therefore, prior to being placed on the wrecker rotation roster, the applicant shall furnish the chief of police with a certificate of insurance that indicates compliance with the following insurance guidelines: 
(1)  Submit a certificate of insurance naming the city police department as the additional insured and stating the city police department will be provided with 30 days' notice of any material change, cancellation or non-renewal. The certificate of insurance should also state that the coverages in subsection (g)(2) of this section are in force. 
(2)  Casualty coverage requirements. 
a.  Not less than $750,000.00 minimum for bodily injury and damage to property in any one accident. 
b.  Not less than $150,000.00 in garage keepers legal liability, which includes fire, explosion, theft, riot and civil commotion, vandalism, collision with a deductible no greater than $500.00. 
(h)  Decal required. A department decal will be placed on each participating wrecker in the lower left corner of the windshield to indicate current inspection and eligibility to participate in the rotation system. Each decal shall indicate the rotation roster permit number and the current calendar year. The fee for each wrecker inspection and issuance of each decal shall be $15.00, and shall be paid by the applicant. 
(i)  Valid license plates requirement. Each wrecker company shall be required to maintain a current, valid license plate on each wrecker used in responding to rotation roster calls. 
(j)  Wrecker company listed only once. Each wrecker company shall be listed on the rotation roster only once. This listing will use the name the wrecker company submitted during the application process and under which he is qualified under this article. It is prohibited for a wrecker company conducting business at one location to receive multiple listings by utilizing a different or fictitious name for wreckers operating from the same location or by utilizing wreckers with the same name out of different locations within the city. Wrecker companies operating more than one rotation wrecker business within the city must maintain completely separate offices, required documentation, logs, and assigned rotation wreckers at the approved locations. A wrecker business will be regarded as having separate locations only when each business or company continuously and regularly occupies separate, different, permanent, nonresidential, non-overlapping structures, each with its own phone number and service, and each keeping its own towing and recovery books, logs, tax records, and other required records, and each business open to customers between the hours of 8:00 a.m. until 5:00 p.m., Monday through Friday. Attempts to circumvent the intent of the rotation system will result in the removal of all wrecker companies and operators associated in any way to the offending wrecker company. 
(k)  Authorization and placement on roster. When the chief of police is satisfied that the applicant has met all requirements, he will place the applicant on the rotation roster and so notify the applicant. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 4, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-85. - Operation and rules of conduct. 
(a)  Obedience to traffic laws. No operator shall speed or violate any other traffic laws or disregard any traffic control devices while answering a call to an accident scene. The provision of the wrecker services shall be done in a reasonable and safe manner, and no operator shall needlessly congest the scene of a traffic accident. While at the scene, the highest ranking city police officer present shall be in charge, and all operators shall follow their direction and commands. 
(b)  Rotation system participation. Authorization to participate in the rotation system shall be considered a personal grant of permission to the wrecker company who made application for the same and shall constitute authorization only to that particular legal entity as it operates a bona fide wrecker service. It shall not be subject to assignment, transfer or lease and neither shall the wrecker company sublet the use of the name under which the rotation system participation was requested and neither shall the operator permit the exercise by another in any manner of the rights or privileges granted by the authorization for participation in the rotation system. Participation on the rotation roster shall not constitute a property interest. Authorization under this article is void if the business address or location of facilities is changed. Further, any change in ownership due to sale, merger, dissolution, death or any other reason shall result in the removal of the wrecker company from the rotation roster and shall necessitate a new application being filed and considered for approval by the chief of police. 
(c)  Submission of daytime and nighttime telephone numbers. At the time of application, each wrecker company shall furnish the chief of police or his designee with one telephone number to be used for dispatches during the day (normal business hours) and one telephone number to be used for dispatches during the night (after normal business hours). Any changes in the aforementioned telephone numbers shall be immediately transmitted to the chief of police or his designee. No pagers or answering machines are permitted to be used as call-out or contact numbers. 
(d)  Twenty-four hour service and access to vehicles. Each wrecker company shall maintain and be fully capable of providing wrecker services 24 hours a day, seven days a week. Further, each wrecker company shall, at no additional cost, provide access, immediately upon request, to its storage facilities between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, to individuals legally entitled or otherwise authorized to view, inspect, access, claim or retrieve personal property or vehicles stored therein. 
(e)  Availability. One attempt by phone shall be made to reach or contact the wrecker company appearing next on the appropriate roster. The acceptance of an assignment may be made by any authorized representative of the company who can verify an immediate dispatch of the wrecker. If no contact is made or the company is unable to accept the call, that company shall be passed for that rotation of the roster and the next wrecker company in line shall be called. A wrecker operator shall not accept a dispatch for wrecker services from the rotation roster unless the operator has a wrecker and the necessary equipment immediately available to perform the requested services. 
(f)  Use of lights. No wrecker operator shall use yellow/amber emergency lights when responding or traveling to a service or wrecker call scene. The use of yellow or amber emergency lighting is authorized only at the scene of an accident or other call for service and when towing or transporting a vehicle from the scene. The use of wig-wag lights is prohibited at all times. 
(g)  Response with own wrecker. The wrecker company shall respond to each dispatch received from the city dispatch with its own wrecker and shall not send another wrecker service in response to a rotation roster dispatch. The responding wrecker must display the name of the wrecker company called by the city dispatcher. In the event the dispatched wrecker is unable to perform the required services or needs of assistance, the police officer has the authorization and discretion to cancel that wrecker and/or dispatch another wrecker service. 
(h)  Response while impaired prohibited. No wrecker operator shall respond to a dispatch when he has consumed alcohol in any amount or has ingested either prescription or non-prescription drugs that may impair motor skills. No wrecker operator shall respond to a dispatch when he is under the influence of any controlled substance. 
(i)  Restriction for conviction of crimes. No wrecker operator shall be on the rotation roster if he has been convicted of any crime within the past five years that is related to his capability to provide wrecker services to the public in a safe and responsible manner. 
(j)  Proficiency. All wrecker operators on the rotation roster shall perform their call-out duty as a wrecker operator in a proficient, professional, polite and competent manner. 
(k)  Driver's license required. No person shall be a wrecker operator or be allowed to drive any wrecker unless such person has a valid state driver's license and a commercial driver's license, if required by law, issued by the state department of public safety. 
(l)  Reflective clothing required. While on the scene of any dispatched scene, all wrecker operators shall wear reflective vests, coats or shirts that meet federal standards as those standards may be amended. 
(m)  Attendance of hazardous material training. All wrecker operators shall make every effort to attend or study some type of hazardous material training with qualified instructors or study material. 
(n)  Removal of glass and debris. Operators shall gather and remove all glass, injurious substances, oil spills, and other debris at or near the scene of the vehicle accident or incident scene with no additional cost as it shall be inclusive within the base price of the tow, unless the debris at accident scene is deemed extreme, unusual or where circumstances would require additional labor to police the debris in a timely manner. 
(o)  Notice of acquisition of a wrecker. Each wrecker company on the rotation roster shall give notice to the chief of police or his designee of any wrecker acquired subsequent to placement on the rotation roster. The police department will inspect the wrecker to determine if it meets all the criteria required by this chapter. No wrecker shall be allowed to perform any rotation roster activity unless properly inspected and decaled in accordance with section 34-84(h). 
(p)  Compliance with laws. Every wrecker company must comply with all applicable federal, state and local laws. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 5, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-86. - Towing and equipment specifications. 
(a)  The minimum standards referred to throughout this article shall be determined solely by the manufacturer's specifications for the capabilities and capacities of the wreckers and all towing equipment. 
(b)  Each wrecker shall be equipped with only those winches and cranes that have been produced and constructed by a manufacturer of such equipment which carries product liability and which regularly produces winches and cranes. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 6, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-87. - Storage procedures. 
(a)  All personal property left in a vehicle and which is unclaimed will be handled in accordance with existing state law. 
(b)  Any person showing proof of identity and showing either proof of ownership or written authorization from the vehicles registered or legal owner may, without charge, inspect the vehicle and remove personal belongings therefrom during normal business hours. For the purposes of this subsection, the term "personal belongings" means those items which belong to the owner, driver or other occupant of the vehicle and which are not attached in any permanent or semi-permanent manner to the interior or exterior of the vehicle. For the purposes of this subsection, the term "permanent or semi-permanent" shall mean that the removal of an attached object would cause physical damage or deformity to the interior or exterior of the vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 7, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-88. - Records. 
(a)  Each operator shall maintain accurate records reflecting all wrecker services performed pursuant to his participation on the wrecker rotation roster. Each record of wrecker service shall include the following information: 
(1)  The date and time the wrecker operator was contacted and was requested to perform the service. 
(2)  The name of the person requesting the service. 
(3)  The location of the vehicle. 
(4)  A description of the towed vehicle, including license plate number and vehicle identification number. 
(5)  The owner or driver of the vehicle, if known. 
(6)  The service charge and itemized fees associated with the tow service. 
(7)  The final disposition of the vehicle. 
Regardless of the method of payment, each customer shall be given a written receipt containing the above-required information, and a copy of the same shall be forwarded to the city police department and the original maintained by the wrecker company. 
(b)  All records required herein must be available immediately upon request so long as the request is made between the hours of 8:00 a.m. until 5:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, for inspection by the chief of police or his designee. Advance notice of an inspection by the chief of police or his designee shall not be required. 
(c)  The operator shall maintain the aforementioned records for the current calendar year and the preceding year. 
(d)  A record of all abandoned motor vehicles is to be maintained by the wrecker company, and any abandoned motor vehicle sold or disposed of by the company shall be so sold or disposed of in accordance with Code of Ala. 1975, § 32-13-1, as may be amended. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 8, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-89. - Rotation roster. 
(a)  A wrecker shall be called from the rotation roster when the following occurs: the owner, driver, or person in charge of a vehicle to be towed has been advised by the officer at the scene that such vehicle must be removed and that he may request the wrecker of his choice. In the event he indicates that he has no preference, or the wrecker of his choice fails to respond to the call within a reasonable period of time considering the time of day, the weather conditions and traffic conditions, the officer shall see that the next wrecker from the appropriate roster shall be called. In no event shall any officer suggest, direct, name or otherwise imply that a particular wrecker be called. 
(b)  A wrecker operator shall promptly respond to a dispatch and arrive on-scene with a fully functional wrecker within 30 minutes under normal driving conditions. If this is not feasible, however, the wrecker operator shall make the same known to the department's communication center and the wrecker company will be passed over for that rotation and dispatch will assign the next wrecker company on the roster. When determining whether a violation of this provision has occurred, the police department shall consider the time of day, the weather conditions and traffic conditions. 
(c)  If a wrecker operator responds to a dispatch, but renders no services through no fault of his own, the wrecker company will not lose position on the rotation roster if the wrecker operator provides prompt notification of the same to the department's communications center. 
(d)  Separate rosters shall be established as follows: All rosters shall be in effect 24 hours a day, seven days a week for assignment by the police department communication center. 
(1)  Regular haul accident rotation (10,000 pounds or less). 
(2)  Heavy haul accident rotation (10,001 pounds or more). 
(3)  Service rotation. 
(4)  Impound rotation. 
(5)  Junk car impoundment rotation (Ordinance Number 415). 
All owners' requests will also be logged accordingly at the police communication center and documented by the investigating officer by utilizing the owners request form. The owners' request form shall be attached to the traffic accident report upon submission to headquarters. 
(e)  If the wrecker operator does not arrive on-scene within the time requirements established herein or if the public health, safety and welfare necessitate more expeditious action, the police department reserves the right to request the services of the next wrecker company on the rotation roster. Under these circumstances, the wrecker company who received the first call will forfeit his position on the rotation roster for that turn. Any wrecker operator who is late in responding to dispatches for wrecker services without justification may be subject to penalties as provided herein. 
(f)  The chief of police or his designee has the right to inspect any wrecker or equipment of a wrecker company on the rotation list. All wreckers and equipment shall be inspected annually by the police department. A current inspection sticker will be issued by the police department and must be displayed as described in section 34-84(h), at all times. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 9, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-90. - Rates and charges. 
(a)  The maximum fees for wrecker services provided by any wrecker service company on the rotation roster in regard to services provided as a result of accident rotation system dispatch shall not exceed the established amounts per wrecker call or incident, unless otherwise and justified by detailed invoice and circumstances. 
(b)  Base price towing services provided hereunder include cleaning of debris from the roadway and roadside, pickup and towing of vehicles to any destination within the city limits to the wrecker company's business location within the city limits; with the exception of the vehicle owner or vehicle owner's designee is making a request to tow the vehicle to another location which may require the negotiation of additional cost agreement between the wrecker company and the owner of the vehicle being towed. 
(c)  Oil dry. The first 40 pounds of oil dry is included in basic towing. Any additional oil dry used may be charged $10.00 per 40-pound bag. 
(1)  Towing of wrecked or disabled vehicles. 
a.  Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,000 pounds or less: $150.00. 
b.  Impoundment: $150.00. 
(2)  Towing of wrecked or disabled vehicles. 
a.  Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,001 pounds through 26,000 pounds: $200.00. 
c.  Impoundment: $200.00. 
(3)  Towing of wrecked or disabled vehicles. 
a.  Two-axle vehicle weighing more than 26,001 pounds or more, or any vehicle with more than two axles: $350.00. 
c.  Impoundment: $350.00. 
(4)  Towing of a wrecked or disabled vehicle with trailer or other vehicle attached in tandem: $75.00 per trailer or vehicle attached in tandem. 
(5)  Towing of wrecked or disabled vehicle attached in tandem, when the tandem trailer or other vehicle exceeds 40 feet in length: $75.00 per trailer or vehicle attached in tandem. Impoundment: $75.00 
(6)  Righting. Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,000 pounds or less: $75.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $75.00 per hour. 
(7)  Righting. Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,001 pounds through 26,000 pounds: $200.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $200.00 per hour. 
(8)  Righting. Two-axle vehicle weighing 26,001 pounds or more, or any vehicle with more than two axles: $350.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $350.00 per hour. 
(9)  Winching. Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,000 pounds or less: $75.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $75.00 per hour. 
(10)  Winching. Two-axle vehicle weighing 10,001 pounds through 26,000 pounds: $200.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $200.00 per hour. 
(11)  Winching. Two-axle vehicle weighing 26,001 pounds or more, or any vehicle with more than two axles: $350.00 for the first hour and prorated in ten minute increments thereafter based on $350.00 per hour. 
For the purposes of this section, the term "winching" means the removal of a vehicle, trailer or other piece of equipment from a location inaccessible to a wrecker to a location where the object of removal is accessible to a wrecker and does not include any incidental or routine winching necessary to load any vehicle onto a wrecker. 
(12)  Righting or lifting by airbag, per pound lifted: $0.035. 
(13)  Forklift, backhoe, track hoe and any other necessary recovery equipment services shall be at commercial rental rates plus ten percent per hour (not including operator). 
(14)  Additional labor: $30.00 per hour. 
For the purpose of this section, the term "additional labor" means additional manpower other than originating wrecker operator and is reserved for traffic accident scenes where extreme circumstances require the removal of wrecked vehicles and/or debris that is too large or difficult for the originating wrecker operator to accomplish alone in a timely manner. 
(15)  Storage rates. 
a.  Passenger vehicle storage rates: 
1.  First 24 hours: No charge. 
2.  Second 24 hours: $30.00. 
3.  Each day thereafter: $30.00. 
b.  Commercial vehicle (vehicles where CDL required) storage rates: 
1.  First 24 hours: No charge. 
2.  Second 24 hours: $50.00. 
3.  Each day thereafter: $50.00. 
(16)  After-hour vehicle release (gate fee): During times other than Monday through Friday, 8:00 a.m. through 5:00 p.m.: $35.00. 
(17)  The rates and charges as established herein do not relate to or regulate consensual wrecker services in which the services for a wrecker company that are chosen by an individual requesting a specific wrecker service (owner requests). 
(Ord. No. 579, § 10, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-91. - Removal from the rotation roster. 
(a)  The city accident and impoundment rotation roster shall be considered and defined as a privilege and not a right. Wrecker companies shall be suspended or removed from the rotation roster for the following reasons: 
(1)  Failure of a wrecker company to meet or follow the requirements established in sections 34-82 through 34-90. 
(2)  Failure to accept or refusal to respond to three calls for service in any 12-month period. 
(b)  After a wrecker company has corrected any violation for which it was suspended or removed, unless the company has been permanently revoked from the program, the wrecker company may reapply for inclusion on the rotation roster using the procedures established in section 34-84. 
(c)  Three suspensions or removals of a wrecker company from the rotation roster, or a felony conviction of the owner or any employee of the wrecker company, or criminal violation related to the wrecker business shall be sufficient grounds for the permanent revocation or suspension of any and all further applications, business licenses and wrecker permits issued to such company by the city. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 11, 11-25-2013) 
Sec. 34-92. - Suspension from the rotation roster. 
(a)  Upon receipt of proof satisfactory to the chief of police or designee, that any wrecker company has violated any of the provisions of this article other than those violations described in section 34-91, or any other ordinance of the city or law of the state or United States, the chief of police may, at his discretion, suspend such wrecker company's name from any or all rotation rosters for such length of time as set forth herein. Suspension hereunder shall be established pursuant to the following criteria: For violations of sections 34-85, 34-89(b) and 34-90 or any violations of this article not specifically covered in aforementioned sections and articles, shall be afforded the same penalties as described as follows:. 
(1)  First violation: 30-day suspension. 
(2)  Second violation: 60-day suspension. 
(3)  Third violation: 90-day suspension. 
(b)  Three suspensions or removals of a wrecker company from the rotation roster within a 12-month period, or a felony conviction of the owner or any employee of the wrecker company, or criminal violation related to the wrecker business shall be sufficient grounds for the permanent revocation or suspension of any and all, further applications and wrecker rotation permits issued to such company by the city. 
(c)  In the event that suspension or revocation of permits or licenses is contemplated against any wrecker company, the police department shall have the authority to require the wrecker company to make available to the chief of police or designee any and all books and records of the wrecker company pursuant to any investigation of violations of this article by the police department. 
(Ord. No. 579, § 12, 11-25-2013) 
Secs. 34-93-34-108. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ABANDONED, WRECKED, STOLEN AND OTHER VEHICLES 

Sec. 34-109. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Property means any real property within the city, or its police jurisdiction, which is not a street or highway. 
    Street or highway means the entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel. 
    Vehicle means a machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners, or slides, and transport persons or property or pull machinery and shall include, without limitation, automobile, truck, trailer, motorcycle, tractor, buggy and wagon. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 1, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-110. - Abandonment of vehicles. 
    No person shall abandon any vehicle within the city. It shall be presumed that any vehicle which has been left at any place on a street or highway within the city for a period of 72 hours consecutively is an abandoned vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 2, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-111. - Leaving of wrecked, non-operating vehicle on street. 
    No person shall leave any partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked, or junked vehicle on any street or highway within the city, except only so long as may be necessitated and required by a wreck, breakdown or other such emergency and subject to the provisions of the preceding section. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 3, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-112. - Disposition of wrecked or discarded vehicles. 
    No person in charge or control of any property within the city, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise, shall allow any partially dismantled, non-operating, wrecked, junked, or discarded vehicle to remain on such property longer than 30 days, and no person shall leave any such vehicle on any property within the city for a longer time than 30 days, except that this article shall not apply with regard to a vehicle in an enclosed building; a vehicle on the premises of a business enterprise operated in a lawful place and manner when necessary to the operation of such business enterprise; or a vehicle in an appropriate storage place or depository maintained in a lawful place and manner by the city. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 4, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-113. - Impounding. 
    The chief of police of the city or any member of his department designated by him is hereby authorized to remove or have removed any vehicle left at any place within the city which reasonably appears to be in violation of this article or lost, stolen, or unclaimed, and the city police department's removal prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived of all such vehicles whose removal would be authorized hereunder is hereby ratified and approved and such vehicles previously so removed and now stored by the city, as well as those which shall hereafter be removed and stored by the city pursuant to this article, shall be disposed of in the manner hereinafter provided. Any vehicle so taken up and removed shall be stored in a suitable place provided by the city to protect it from deterioration. A permanent record giving the date of the taking of each vehicle, the place where found and taken, and a description of the vehicle shall be kept by the chief of police of the city. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 5, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-114. - Sale. 
    At least every six months, the chief of police of the city shall sell at public auction to the highest bidder for cash the vehicle or vehicles herein authorized to be removed and taken up and which shall have been taken up and stored for a period of three months or more, the sales to be made after notice of the time and place therefor shall have first been given by publication once a week for two successive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation published in the city. The first publication shall be at least 20 days before the sale. Each vehicle shall be sold separately and a notation in the storage record book shall be made of the amount received for each vehicle. The person making the sale shall have the right to reject any and all bids if the amount bid be unreasonably low and shall have the right to continue the sales from time to time if no bidders are present. After deducting and paying all expenses incurred in the removal, taking up, storing, maintaining and selling, of the vehicle or vehicles, the balance if any shall be paid into the general fund of the city. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 6, 3-8-1971) 
Sec. 34-115. - Redemption. 
    The owner of any vehicle taken up and stored as herein provided may redeem the same at any time prior to its sale by paying the reasonable expense of taking the vehicle in charge, its maintenance and storage and a prorate of the cost of publication. 
(Ord. No. 92, § 7, 3-8-1971) 
Chapter 36 - UTILITIES 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 36-1-36-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SEWER USE 

Sec. 36-19. - Abbreviations and definitions. 
(a)  The following abbreviations shall have the designated meanings: 
Abbreviation Meaning AWIC Alabama Water Improvement Commission BOD Biochemical oxygen demand CFR Code of Federal Regulations EPA United States Environmental Protection Agency NPDES National pollutant discharge elimination system OSHA Occupational Safety and Health Administration P.L. Public Law POTW Publicly owned treatment works SS Suspended solids  
(b)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Act or the Act means the Federal Water Pollution Control Act (P.L. 92-500) as amended by the Clean Water Act of 1977 (P.L. 95-217), and as further amended. 
    Approval authority means the director of the Alabama Water Improvement Commission (AWIC). 
    Authorized representative of industrial user means: 
(1)  A principal executive officer of at least the level of vice-president if the industrial user is a corporation. 
(2)  A general partner or proprietor if the industrial user is a partnership or proprietorship, respectively. 
(3)  A duly authorized representative of the individual designated above if such representative is responsible for the overall operation of the facilities from which the indirect discharge originates. 
    Biochemical oxygen demand or BOD means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedures in five days at 20 degrees Celsius (68 degrees Fahrenheit) expressed in terms of weight and concentration (milligrams per liter). 
    Board means the water works, sewer and gas board of the city. 
    Building sewer or house connection means the connecting pipe from a building to the sanitary sewer. 
    City clerk means the administrative officer of the city council who is charged with administrative duties by the council and is responsible directly to the council as used herein. The term "city clerk" may also include any other employee of the city delegated to act for the council by the city clerk or by the council. 
    Combined sewer means a sewer receiving both surface runoff and waste water. 
    Cooling water means the water discharged from any use such as air conditioning, cooling or refrigeration, or to which the only pollutant added is heat. 
    Direct discharge means the discharge of treated or untreated wastewater directly to the waters of the state. 
    Domestic wastewater means all liquid and waterborne pollutants, exclusive of unpolluted water as defined in this section or wastewater or wastes from processes or operations of industrial users as defined in this section. 
    Environmental Protection Agency or EPA means the United States Environmental Protection Agency or, where appropriate, the term "Environmental Protection Agency" may also be used as a designation for the administrator or other duly authorized official of said agency. 
    Holding tank waste means any waste from holding tanks such as vessels, chemical toilets, campers, trailers, septic tanks, vacuum-pump tank trucks, and septic tank haulers. 
    Indirect discharge means the discharge or the introduction of non-domestic pollutants from any source regulated under section 307(b) or (c) of the Act into the sewerage system (including holding tank waste discharged into the sewerage system). 
    Industrial user means any user of the sewerage system who is a source of indirect discharge which does not constitute a discharge of pollutants under regulations issued pursuant to section 402 of the Act. (A user who discharges industrial waste into the sewerage system.) 
    Industrial waste means the liquid or other wastes resulting from any process of industry, manufacture, trade or business or from the development of natural resources. 
    Manager means the administrative officer of the water works, sewer and gas board of the city who is charged with administrative control of all operations of the board and is responsible directly to the board. As used herein, the term "manager" may also include any other board employee delegated to act for the board by the manager or by the board. 
    National pollutant discharge elimination system permit or NPDES permit means a permit to discharge wastewater issued pursuant to section 402 of the Act. 
    Person means any individual, firm company, association, corporation, governmental agency, board, commission, or municipal corporation other than the city. 
    Pollution means the manmade or man-induced alteration of the chemical, physical, biological, and/or radiological integrity of water. 
    Pollutant means any solid waste, chemical waste, biological material, radioactive material, thermal waste, or industrial, municipal, or agricultural waste discharged into water. 
    Private wastewater disposal system means any facilities for wastewater treatment and disposal not maintained and operated by the city. 
    Properly shredded garbage means the organic wastes resulting from the preparation, cooking, and dispensing of foods that have been shredded to such degree that all particles will be carried freely under flow conditions normally prevailing in public sewers, with no particle being greater than one-half inch in any dimension. 
    Public sewer means a sewer in which all owners of abutting properties shall have equal rights, and which is controlled by a governmental agency or public utility. 
    Publicly owned treatment works or POTW means as defined by section 212 of the Act, which are owned in this instance by the city or the board. This definition includes the wastewater treatment plant and any sewers that convey wastewater to the wastewater treatment plant (sewerage system). 
    Receiving stream means that body of water, stream, or watercourse receiving the discharge from a wastewater treatment plant or that body of water, stream, or watercourse formed by the effluent from a wastewater treatment plant. 
    Sanitary sewage means sewage excluding process wastes from industrial users. 
    Sanitary sewer means a public sewer controlled by a governmental agency or public utility that carries liquid and waterborne wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants, and institutions, together with minor quantities of groundwaters and surface waters that are not admitted intentionally. 
    Sewage means a combination of water-carried wastes from residences and industrial users (waste water). 
    Sewer means a pipe or conduit for carrying waste water. 
    Sewerage system means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of wastewater (POTW). 
    Shall; may. The term "shall" is mandatory; the term "may" is permissible. 
    Significant industrial user means any industrial user of the city sewerage system who: 
(1)  Has a discharge flow of 25,000 gallons or more per average work day. 
(2)  Has a discharge which is greater than five percent of the hydraulic flow or organic design capacity of the city sewerage system. 
(3)  Has a discharge which contains toxic pollutants or priority pollutants as defined pursuant to section 307 of the Act or state statutes and rules and regulations. 
(4)  Is found by the water works, sewer and gas board of the city, the approval authority or EPA to have significant impact, either singly or in combination with other contributing industries, on the sewerage system, the quality of sludge, the system's effluent quality, or air emissions generated by the sewerage system. 
    Storm sewer or storm drain means a sewer which carries stormwater and surface waters and drainage, but which excludes sanitary sewage and polluted industrial wastes. 
    Stormwater means any flow occurring during or following any form of natural precipitation and resulting therefrom. 
    Suspended solids means the total solid matter that either floats on the surface of or is suspended in water or liquid waste and which is removable by laboratory filtration. 
    Unpolluted waste water. 
(1)  The term "unpolluted waste water" means any wastewater which is substantially free of pollutants and is discharged from the following: 
a.  Rain downspouts and drains. 
b.  Footing drains. 
c.  Stormwater and surface water drains. 
d.  Cooling water systems. 
(2)  The term "unpolluted waste water" shall contain, by definition, none of the following: 
a.  BOD in excess of ten mg/l. 
b.  Suspended solids in excess of ten mg/l. 
c.  Free or emulsified greases or oils. 
d.  Acids or alkalies. 
e.  Phenols or other substances imparting taste or odor to receiving waters. 
f.  Toxic or poisonous substances. 
g.  Noxious or odorous gases. 
h.  Any wastewater with a temperature which exceeds 60 degrees Celsius (140 degrees Fahrenheit) at its introduction into the sewerage system or which exceeds 40 degrees Celsius (104 degrees Fahrenheit) at its introduction into a wastewater treatment plant or a receiving stream. 
    User means any person who contributes, causes or permits the contribution of wastewater into the sewerage system. 
    Wastewater treatment plant means the facilities of the city, or the board, for treating and disposing of waste water. 
    Water works, sewer and gas board or board means the water works, sewer and gas board of the city or, where appropriate, the terms "water works," "sewer and gas board" or "board" may also be used as a designation for the manager or other duly authorized official of the board. 
    Watercourse means a channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or intermittently. 
    Waters of the state means all bodies or accumulations of water, surface or underground, within the boundaries of the state. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 1, 7-8-1985) 
Sec. 36-20. - Use of public sewers required. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to place, deposit, or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary manner on public or private property within the city or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any human excrement, garbage, or other objectionable waste. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge to any outlet other than a sanitary sewer, within the corporate limits, any domestic or industrial wastes except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent provisions of this article and regulations of the city waterworks and sewer board and where an appropriate NPDES permit has been obtained from AWIC pursuant to section 402 of the Act. 
(c)  Where a storm sewer, as defined by section 36-19(b), is adjacent to a property, it shall be legal to discharge cooling water, as defined by section 36-19(b) and which meets the requirements of section 36-19(b), into said storm sewer in accordance with subsequent provisions of this article and where the city determines that sufficient capacity exists in said storm sewer to carry the cooling water without exceeding the design storm drainage capacity of said storm sewer, and where an appropriate NPDES permit has been obtained from AWIC pursuant to section 402 of the Act. 
(d)  Connections required within specified distance. 
(1)  The owners of all houses, buildings, or properties used for human occupancy, situated within the city and abutting on any public street, alley, or right-of-way in which there is now located or may in the future be located within 250 feet of said house, building, or property used for human occupancy a public sanitary sewer of the city that discharges to the city wastewater treatment plant, is hereby required at the owner's expense to connect such house, building, or property used for human occupancy directly with the proper public sanitary sewer in accordance with the provisions of this article and regulations of the water works, sewer and gas board within 180 days after the date of official notice to do so. These connections shall be made in accordance with the provisions of this article and regulations of the board. 
(2)  The owners of all buildings or properties used for employment, recreation, or other nonresidential purposes, situated within the city and abutting on any street, alley, or right-of-way in which there is now located or may in the future be located within 100 feet of said property, a public sanitary sewer of the city that discharges to the city wastewater treatment plant, who have installed suitable toilet and other facilities therein necessary for the discharge of domestic and/or industrial waste, are hereby required, at the owner's expense, to connect such facilities directly with the proper public sanitary sewer in accordance with the provisions of this article and regulations of the water works, sewer and gas board within 180 days after the date of the official notice to do so. These connections shall be made in accordance with the provisions of section 36-22 and the regulations of the board. 
(e)  Properties and connections outside the required distance. 
(1)  In the event the owner of a house, building, or property used for human occupancy which is or becomes available to a public sanitary sewer by virtue of being within 250 feet of said residence, does not cause the required connection of such property to the sewerage system to be made within the 180-day period after official notice to do so has been given by the board, the water works, sewer and gas board shall be authorized, on behalf of the city, to give another final written notice to such owner to connect such property to the sewerage system. In the event that such owner fails or refuses to connect such house, building, or property used for human occupancy to the sewerage system within ten days following such date that the final written notice is given, such house, building, or property used for human occupancy shall be subject to and shall thereafter be billed for the monthly sewerage charge by the board following such ten-day notice, and a failure to pay such monthly sewerage charge within the normal time allowed to sewer customers by the board's regulations shall subject the house, building, or property used for human occupancy and the owner and/or occupant thereof to the same sanctions and treatments by the board as would be applicable to other sewer customers who are delinquent in the payment of their sewer bills. 
(2)  In the event the owner of any property used for employment, recreation, or other nonresidential purposes which is or becomes available to a public sanitary sewer, by virtue of being within 100 feet herebefore specified, does not cause the required connection of such property to the sewerage system to be made within the 180-day period after the date of official notice to do so has been given by the board, the board shall give another final written notice to such owner to connect such property to the sewerage system. In the event that such owner fails or refuses to connect such property to the sewerage system within ten days following such date that the final written notice is given, such unconnected property shall be subject to and shall thereafter be billed for the monthly sewerage charge by the board following such ten-day notice, and a failure to pay such monthly sewer charges within the normal time allowed to sewer customers by the board's regulations shall subject the property in question and the owner and/or occupant thereof to the same sanctions and treatment by the board as would be applicable to other sewer customers who are delinquent in the payment of their sewer bills. 
(f)  In the event the owner of any property to whom the notice provided under subsection (e) of this section is required to be given is a nonresident, notice shall be given to such owner by publication once a week for three consecutive weeks in a newspaper published in the city by mailing a copy of such notice to such owner at his last known address, and by delivering a copy of such notice to the agent or occupant of such property. Whenever any notice to a resident owner of property available to sewers is returned "Not Found" the water works, sewer and gas board may prescribe alias notices to be served as in the case of the original notice; two returns of "Not Found" to such a resident owner shall authorize the board to proceed to give notice to such resident owner in a manner provided in the preceding sentence for nonresident owners of property available to sewers. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 2, 7-8-1985; Ord. No. 335, § 1, 3-11-1992; Ord. No. 418, § 1(a)-(c), (e), 7-14-1997) 
Sec. 36-21. - Private wastewater disposal. 
(a)  Where a public sanitary sewer is not available under the provisions of section 36-20, such toilet and other facilities necessary for the discharge of domestic and/or industrial wastes shall be connected to a private wastewater disposal system complying with the requirements of the state, the county and/or the city, and provisions of the International Plumbing Code in force in the city. 
(b)  Before commencement of construction of a private wastewater disposal system, the owners shall first obtain a written permit from the appropriate regulatory authority and furnish a copy thereof to the city. The copy of the permit shall be accompanied by such supplementary data as deemed necessary by the city to maintain an accurate file of such private wastewater disposal systems to facilitate the planning of future public sewer service. 
(c)  The type, capacity, location, and layout of a private wastewater disposal system, including methods of sludge disposal, shall comply with all requirements of the state, the county and/or the city. 
(d)  At such time as public sewer becomes available within 250 feet of a house, building, or property used for human occupancy or within 100 feet of a property used for employment, recreation, or other nonresidential purposes served by a private wastewater disposal system, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer within 180 days in compliance with this article and the regulations of the water works, sewer and gas board of the city; and any septic tanks, cesspools, and similar private wastewater disposal facilities shall be cleaned of sludge and filled with suitable material. 
(e)  The owners shall operate and maintain any private wastewater disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no expense to the city. 
(f)  No person shall discharge any holding tank wastes or septic tank wastes from private systems into the sewerage system without an appropriate permit from the water works, sewer and gas board of the city. All such discharges shall be in accordance with the regulations of the board. 
(g)  No statement contained in this section shall be construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed by federal or state agencies. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 3, 7-8-1985; Ord. No. 418, § 1(d), 7-14-1997) 
Sec. 36-22. - Building sewers, connections and permits. 
(a)  No unauthorized persons shall uncover, make any connections with or opening into, use, alter, or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the water works, sewer and gas board of the city. 
(b)  All costs and expenses incidental to the installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owners. The owners shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may be directly or indirectly occasioned by the installation of the building sewer. 
(c)  A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building; except where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard, or driveway, the building sewer for the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer, but the city does not and will not assume any obligation or responsibility for damage caused by or resulting from any such single connection aforementioned. 
(d)  Existing building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they are found on examination and test by the board to meet all the requirements of this article. 
(e)  The size, slope, alignment, materials of construction of a building sewer, and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, jointing, testing, and back-filling the trench, shall all conform to the requirements of the southern building code or other applicable rules and regulations of the board. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the ASTM and WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply. 
(f)  Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and discharged to the building sewer. 
(g)  The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall conform to the requirements of the southern building code or other applicable rules and regulations of the city, or the procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the ASTM and the WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9. All such connections shall be made gastight and watertight and verified by proper testing. Any deviation from the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the city before installation. 
(h)  The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the board when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection to the public sewer. The connection and testing shall be made under the supervision of the board. 
(i)  All excavations for building sewer installations shall be adequately guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazards. Streets, sidewalks, parkways, and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the board and the city. 
(j)  All construction activities shall conform to all applicable OSHA regulations. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 4, 7-8-1985) 
Sec. 36-23. - Protection of equipment. 
    Only persons authorized by the water works, sewer and gas board of the city or AWIC will be allowed to uncover, adjust, maintain, and remove such equipment and materials. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 5, 7-8-1985) 
Sec. 36-24. - Violations and penalties. 
    A violation of or failure to comply with any of the provisions of this article, including the willful furnishing of false information relative to same for the use of the sewerage system, shall be and hereby is declared to be a misdemeanor. Every person concerned in the violation of the provisions of this article or failure to comply with same, or who furnishes false information relative to his use of the sewerage system aforesaid, whether he directly commits the acts or aids and abets same, and whether present or absent, shall be proceeded against and held as a principal. 
(Ord. No. 241, § 6, 7-8-1985) 
Appendix A - ZONING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Printed in this appendix is the city's zoning ordinance, being Ord. No. 558, adopted on July 26, 2010. Amendments are indicated by parenthetical history notes following amended provisions. The absence of a history note indicates that the provision remains unchanged from the original. Obvious misspellings and punctuation errors have been corrected without notation. For stylistic purposes, headings and catchlines have been made uniform and the same system of capitalization and expression of numbers in text as appears in the Code of Ordinances has been used. Additions made for clarity are shown in brackets. 
State Law reference- Zoning, Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-52-70 et seq. 

ARTICLE 1. - TITLE, LEGAL STATUS PROVISIONS AND OFFICIAL ZONING MAP 

Sec. 1.1. - Title. 
    This ordinance shall be known and may be cited as "the zoning ordinance of the City of Scottsboro, Alabama." 
Sec. 1.2. - Short title. 
    This ordinance and all subsequent amendments, attachments, and supplements thereto shall be known as the "Scottsboro zoning ordinance." 
Sec. 1.3. - Legal status provisions. 
1.3.1.  Authority. This ordinance has been drafted, subjected to public review, recommended by the Scottsboro Planning Commission, and adopted by the Scottsboro City Council under the authority of title 11, chapter 52 of the Code of Alabama, 1975 Compilation, as amended [Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-52-1 et seq.]. 
1.3.2.  Purpose. The purpose of this ordinance is to guide development within the City of Scottsboro in accordance with title 11, chapter 52 of the Code of Alabama, 1975 Compilation, as amended [Code of Ala. 1975, § 11-52-1 et seq.]; and generally to implement and support the developmental policies of the City of Scottsboro. 
1.3.3.  Interpretation. In interpreting and applying the provisions of this ordinance, they shall be held to be the minimum requirements for the promotion of the public safety, health, convenience, comfort, prosperity, and general welfare. 
1.3.4.  Conflict with other ordinances. In case of a conflict between this ordinance or any part thereof, and the whole or part of any existing or future ordinance of the city, the most restrictive shall in all cases apply. 
1.3.5.  Validity, severability. If any article, section, subsection, paragraph, item or any provision of this ordinance shall be held to be invalid or unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, such holding shall not affect any other article, section, subsection, or part thereof of this ordinance which is not of itself invalid or unconstitutional. 
1.3.6.  Repeal of conflicting ordinances. On the effective date of this ordinance, all other local ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict or inconsistent with this ordinance, and all amendments thereto, are hereby repealed to the extent necessary to give this ordinance full force and effect. 
Sec. 1.4. - Official zoning map. 
    The city is hereby divided into zones or districts, as shown on the official zoning map which, together with all explanatory matter thereon, is hereby adopted by reference and declared to be a part of this ordinance. 
1.4.1.  The official zoning map shall be identified by the signature of the mayor attested by the city clerk, and bearing the seal of the city under the following words: "This is to certify that this is the official zoning map of the City of Scottsboro, Alabama," together with the date of the adoption of this ordinance. 
1.4.2.  If changes are made in district boundaries or other matter portrayed on the official zoning map, such changes shall be entered promptly after the amendment has been approved by the city council, hereinafter referred to as "the council." No amendment to this ordinance shall become effective until after such change and entry has been made on said map. 
1.4.3.  No changes of any nature shall be made on the official zoning map or matter shown thereon, except in conformity with the procedures set forth in this ordinance. Any unauthorized changes of whatever kind by any person or persons shall be considered a violation of this ordinance and punishable as described herein. 
1.4.4.  Regardless of the existence of purported copies of the official zoning map, which may from time-to-time be published, the official zoning map shall be located in the office of the city clerk and shall be the final authority as to the current zoning status of land and water areas, building, and other structures in the city. 
1.4.5.  Replacement of the official zoning map. 
1.  In the event that the official zoning map becomes damaged, destroyed, lost, or difficult to interpret because of the nature or number of changes and additions, the council may, by resolution, adopt a new official zoning map, which shall supersede the prior official zoning map. The new official zoning map may correct drafting or other errors or omissions on the prior official zoning map, but no such corrections shall have the effect of amending the original official zoning map or any subsequent amendment thereof. The new official zoning map shall be identified by the signature of the mayor attested by the city clerk, and bearing the seal of the city under the following words: "This is to certify that this official zoning map supersedes and replaces the official zoning map adopted (date of adoption of map being replaced) as part of the zoning ordinance." 
2.  Unless the prior official zoning map has been lost or has been totally destroyed, the prior map or any significant parts thereof remaining shall be preserved, together with all available records pertaining to its adoption or amendment. 
Sec. 1.5. - Using this ordinance. 
1.5.1.  Internal referencing. All references to articles, sections, subsections, paragraphs and items within this ordinance shall refer to articles, sections, subsections, paragraphs and items in this ordinance unless otherwise specified. When an article, section or other subdivision is referenced within a provision or requirement of this ordinance, unless otherwise specified, all subdivisions within such reference shall be assumed to be applicable. 
1.5.2.  Page numbering. Each article contains its own separate page numbering system. The page numbers are prefixed by the respective article number. As an example, page 10 of article 8 is designated page 8-10. 
Editor's note- Subsection 1.5.2 is incorrect given the page numbering scheme used in this publication. 
ARTICLE 2. - DEFINITIONS 
    For the purposes of this ordinance, certain terms or words used herein shall be interpreted as follows: 

Sec. 2.1. - Interpretation. 
2.1.1.  The word "used" or "occupied" as applied to any land or building shall be construed to include the words "intended, arranged, or designed to be used or occupied." 
2.1.2.  The word "building" includes "structure." 
2.1.3.  The word "person" includes a firm, association, organization, partnership, trust, company, or corporation as well as an individual. 
2.1.4.  The present tense includes the future tense, the singular number includes the plural, and the plural number includes the singular. 
2.1.5.  The masculine gender shall include the feminine, and the feminine gender shall include the masculine. 
2.1.6.  The word "shall" is mandatory; the word "may" is permissive. 
2.1.7.  The word "lot" includes the words "plot" or "parcel." 
2.1.8.  Except as otherwise, provided herein, all words have their customary dictionary meaning. The zoning official is authorized to make a final determination of the meaning of any term used in this ordinance, which determination may be appealed to the board. 
Sec. 2.2. - Definitions of terms used in this ordinance. 
2.2.1.  Abutting: Touching along a common side, boundary or property line. Two pieces of property that are separated by a right-of-way are "adjacent," but not "abutting." 
2.2.2.  Access: A way or means of approach to provide physical entrance to a property. 
2.2.3.  Accessory structure or accessory building: A structure on the same lot with, and of a nature customarily incidental and subordinate to, the principal structure. 
2.2.4.  Accessory use: A use of land or of a building or portion thereof commonly associated with and integrally related to the principal use of the land or building on the same lot. 
2.2.5.  Adjacent: Either abutting or on the opposite side of a street, right-of-way, or easement that separates it from the subject property. Properties separated by a railroad shall not be considered "adjacent." 
2.2.6.  Adjoining: See "Abutting." 
2.2.7.  Agriculture: The production, storage, keeping, harvesting, grading, packaging, processing, boarding or maintenance, for sale, lease, or personal use, of plants and animals, including, but not limited to: forages and sod crops; grains and seed crops; dairy animals and products; poultry and poultry products; the keeping, raising and breeding of livestock; bees and apiary products; fur animals; trees and forest products; fruits, nuts and vegetables; plants and flowers; or lands that are devoted to soil conservation or forestry management. 
2.2.8.  Alley: A public or private way, other than a driveway, less in width than a street, designed for the special accommodation of the property it reaches, and not intended for general circulation. 
2.2.9.  Alteration: Any change or rearrangement in the supporting members of an existing building, such as bearing walls, columns, beams, girders or interior partitions, as well as any change in doors or windows or any enlargement to a building or structure, whether horizontally or vertically, or the moving of a building or structure from one location to another. 
2.2.10.  Animal shelter: A nonprofit or public facility providing shelter for small domestic animals. 
2.2.11.  Applicable district: That zoning district in which a building, structure, property, or subdivision, for which a zoning application is submitted or permit is sought, is located or is to be moved. 
2.2.12.  Applicant: A person submitting an application for development, variance, special, exception, conditional use or rezoning. 
2.2.13.  Assisted living facility: A building, portion of a building, or a group of buildings in which room, board, meals, laundry, and assistance with personal care and other services are, provided for not less than 24 hours in any week to at least two ambulatory adults not related by blood or marriage to the owner and/or administrator and licensed by the State of Alabama. 
2.2.14.
